"146" "ADVENTURES OF SHERLOCK HOLMES"
"147" ""
"148" "Adventure I"
"149" ""
"150" "A SCANDAL IN BOHEMIA"
"151" ""
"152" ""
"153" "I"
"154" ""
"155" "To Sherlock Holmes she is always _the_ woman. I have seldom heard"
"156" "him mention her under any other name. In his eyes she eclipses and"
"157" "predominates the whole of her sex. It was not that he felt any emotion"
"158" "akin to love for Irene Adler. All emotions, and that one particularly,"
"159" "were abhorrent to his cold, precise, but admirably balanced mind. He"
"160" "was, I take it, the most perfect reasoning and observing machine that"
"161" "the world has seen; but, as a lover, he would have placed himself in a"
"162" "false position. He never spoke of the softer passions, save with a gibe"
"163" "and a sneer. They were admirable things for the observer—excellent"
"164" "for drawing the veil from men’s motives and actions. But for the"
"165" "trained reasoner to admit such intrusions into his own delicate and"
"166" "finely adjusted temperament was to introduce a distracting factor which"
"167" "might throw a doubt upon all his mental results. Grit in a sensitive"
"168" "instrument, or a crack in one of his own high-power lenses, would not"
"169" "be more disturbing than a strong emotion in a nature such as his. And"
"170" "yet there was but one woman to him, and that woman was the late Irene"
"171" "Adler, of dubious and questionable memory."
"172" ""
"173" "I had seen little of Holmes lately. My marriage had drifted us away"
"174" "from each other. My own complete happiness, and the home-centred"
"175" "interests which rise up around the man who first finds himself master"
"176" "of his own establishment, were sufficient to absorb all my attention;"
"177" "while Holmes, who loathed every form of society with his whole"
"178" "Bohemian soul, remained in our lodgings in Baker Street, buried among"
"179" "his old books, and alternating from week to week between cocaine and"
"180" "ambition, the drowsiness of the drug, and the fierce energy of his"
"181" "own keen nature. He was still, as ever, deeply attracted by the study"
"182" "of crime, and occupied his immense faculties and extraordinary powers"
"183" "of observation in following out those clues, and clearing up those"
"184" "mysteries, which had been abandoned as hopeless by the official police."
"185" "From time to time I heard some vague account of his doings: of his"
"186" "summons to Odessa in the case of the Trepoff murder, of his clearing"
"187" "up of the singular tragedy of the Atkinson brothers at Trincomalee,"
"188" "and finally of the mission which he had accomplished so delicately and"
"189" "successfully for the reigning family of Holland. Beyond these signs of"
"190" "his activity, however, which I merely shared with all the readers of"
"191" "the daily press, I knew little of my former friend and companion."
"192" ""
"193" "One night—it was on the 20th of March, 1888—I was returning from a"
"194" "journey to a patient (for I had now returned to civil practice), when"
"195" "my way led me through Baker Street. As I passed the well-remembered"
"196" "door, which must always be associated in my mind with my wooing, and"
"197" "with the dark incidents of the Study in Scarlet, I was seized with a"
"198" "keen desire to see Holmes again, and to know how he was employing his"
"199" "extraordinary powers. His rooms were brilliantly lit, and, even as I"
"200" "looked up, I saw his tall, spare figure pass twice in a dark silhouette"
"201" "against the blind. He was pacing the room swiftly, eagerly, with his"
"202" "head sunk upon his chest and his hands clasped behind him. To me, who"
"203" "knew his every mood and habit, his attitude and manner told their own"
"204" "story. He was at work again. He had arisen out of his drug-created"
"205" "dreams, and was hot upon the scent of some new problem. I rang the"
"206" "bell, and was shown up to the chamber which had formerly been in part"
"207" "my own."
"208" ""
"209" "His manner was not effusive. It seldom was; but he was glad, I think,"
"210" "to see me. With hardly a word spoken, but with a kindly eye, he waved"
"211" "me to an arm-chair, threw across his case of cigars, and indicated a"
"212" "spirit case and a gasogene in the corner. Then he stood before the"
"213" "fire, and looked me over in his singular introspective fashion."
"214" ""
"215" "“Wedlock suits you,” he remarked. “I think, Watson, that you have put"
"216" "on seven and a half pounds since I saw you.”"
"217" ""
"218" "“Seven!” I answered."
"219" ""
"220" "“Indeed, I should have thought a little more. Just a trifle more, I"
"221" "fancy, Watson. And in practice again, I observe. You did not tell me"
"222" "that you intended to go into harness.”"
"223" ""
"224" "“Then, how do you know?”"
"225" ""
"226" "“I see it, I deduce it. How do I know that you have been getting"
"227" "yourself very wet lately, and that you have a most clumsy and careless"
"228" "servant girl?”"
"229" ""
"230" "“My dear Holmes,” said I, “this is too much. You would certainly have"
"231" "been burned, had you lived a few centuries ago. It is true that I had"
"232" "a country walk on Thursday and came home in a dreadful mess; but, as I"
"233" "have changed my clothes, I can’t imagine how you deduce it. As to Mary"
"234" "Jane, she is incorrigible, and my wife has given her notice; but there,"
"235" "again, I fail to see how you work it out.”"
"236" ""
"237" "He chuckled to himself and rubbed his long, nervous hands together."
"238" ""
"239" "“It is simplicity itself,” said he; “my eyes tell me that on the"
"240" "inside of your left shoe, just where the firelight strikes it, the"
"241" "leather is scored by six almost parallel cuts. Obviously they have"
"242" "been caused by some one who has very carelessly scraped round the"
"243" "edges of the sole in order to remove crusted mud from it. Hence, you"
"244" "see, my double deduction that you had been out in vile weather, and"
"245" "that you had a particularly malignant boot-slitting specimen of the"
"246" "London slavey. As to your practice, if a gentleman walks into my rooms"
"247" "smelling of iodoform, with a black mark of nitrate of silver upon his"
"248" "right forefinger, and a bulge on the side of his top-hat to show where"
"249" "he has secreted his stethoscope, I must be dull, indeed, if I do not"
"250" "pronounce him to be an active member of the medical profession.”"
"251" ""
"252" "I could not help laughing at the ease with which he explained his"
"253" "process of deduction. “When I hear you give your reasons,” I remarked,"
"254" "“the thing always appears to me to be so ridiculously simple that I"
"255" "could easily do it myself, though at each successive instance of your"
"256" "reasoning I am baffled, until you explain your process. And yet I"
"257" "believe that my eyes are as good as yours.”"
"258" ""
"259" "“Quite so,” he answered, lighting a cigarette, and throwing himself"
"260" "down into an arm-chair. “You see, but you do not observe. The"
"261" "distinction is clear. For example, you have frequently seen the steps"
"262" "which lead up from the hall to this room.”"
"263" ""
"264" "“Frequently.”"
"265" ""
"266" "“How often?”"
"267" ""
"268" "“Well, some hundreds of times.”"
"269" ""
"270" "“Then how many are there?”"
"271" ""
"272" "“How many? I don’t know.”"
"273" ""
"274" "“Quite so! You have not observed. And yet you have seen. That is just"
"275" "my point. Now, I know that there are seventeen steps, because I have"
"276" "both seen and observed. By-the-way, since you are interested in these"
"277" "little problems, and since you are good enough to chronicle one or two"
"278" "of my trifling experiences, you may be interested in this.” He threw"
"279" "over a sheet of thick, pink-tinted note-paper which had been lying open"
"280" "upon the table. “It came by the last post,” said he. “Read it aloud.”"
"281" ""
"282" "The note was undated, and without either signature or address."
"283" ""
"284" "“There will call upon you to-night, at a quarter to eight o’clock,”"
"285" "it said, “a gentleman who desires to consult you upon a matter of the"
"286" "very deepest moment. Your recent services to one of the royal houses"
"287" "of Europe have shown that you are one who may safely be trusted with"
"288" "matters which are of an importance which can hardly be exaggerated."
"289" "This account of you we have from all quarters received. Be in your"
"290" "chamber then at that hour, and do not take it amiss if your visitor"
"291" "wear a mask.”"
"292" ""
"293" "“This is indeed a mystery,” I remarked. “What do you imagine that it"
"294" "means?”"
"295" ""
"296" "“I have no data yet. It is a capital mistake to theorize before one has"
"297" "data. Insensibly one begins to twist facts to suit theories, instead of"
"298" "theories to suit facts. But the note itself. What do you deduce from"
"299" "it?”"
"300" ""
"301" "I carefully examined the writing, and the paper upon which it was"
"302" "written."
"303" ""
"304" "“The man who wrote it was presumably well to do,” I remarked,"
"305" "endeavoring to imitate my companion’s processes. “Such paper could not"
"306" "be bought under half a crown a packet. It is peculiarly strong and"
"307" "stiff.”"
"308" ""
"309" "“Peculiar—that is the very word,” said Holmes. “It is not an English"
"310" "paper at all. Hold it up to the light.”"
"311" ""
"312" "I did so, and saw a large _E_ with a small _g_, a _P_, and a large _G_"
"313" "with a small _t_ woven into the texture of the paper."
"314" ""
"315" "“What do you make of that?” asked Holmes."
"316" ""
"317" "“The name of the maker, no doubt; or his monogram, rather.”"
"318" ""
"319" "“Not at all. The _G_ with the small _t_ stands for ‘Gesellschaft,’"
"320" "which is the German for ‘Company.’ It is a customary contraction like"
"321" "our ‘Co.’ _P_, of course, stands for ‘Papier.’ Now for the _Eg_. Let us"
"322" "glance at our Continental Gazetteer.” He took down a heavy brown volume"
"323" "from his shelves. “Eglow, Eglonitz—here we are, Egria. It is in a"
"324" "German-speaking country—in Bohemia, not far from Carlsbad. ‘Remarkable"
"325" "as being the scene of the death of Wallenstein, and for its numerous"
"326" "glass-factories and paper-mills.’ Ha, ha, my boy, what do you make of"
"327" "that?” His eyes sparkled, and he sent up a great blue triumphant cloud"
"328" "from his cigarette."
"329" ""
"330" "“The paper was made in Bohemia,” I said."
"331" ""
"332" "“Precisely. And the man who wrote the note is a German. Do you note the"
"333" "peculiar construction of the sentence—‘This account of you we have"
"334" "from all quarters received.’ A Frenchman or Russian could not have"
"335" "written that. It is the German who is so uncourteous to his verbs. It"
"336" "only remains, therefore, to discover what is wanted by this German"
"337" "who writes upon Bohemian paper, and prefers wearing a mask to showing"
"338" "his face. And here he comes, if I am not mistaken, to resolve all our"
"339" "doubts.”"
"340" ""
"341" "As he spoke there was the sharp sound of horses’ hoofs and grating"
"342" "wheels against the curb, followed by a sharp pull at the bell. Holmes"
"343" "whistled."
"344" ""
"345" "“A pair, by the sound,” said he. “Yes,” he continued, glancing out of"
"346" "the window. “A nice little brougham and a pair of beauties. A hundred"
"347" "and fifty guineas apiece. There’s money in this case, Watson, if there"
"348" "is nothing else.”"
"349" ""
"350" "“I think that I had better go, Holmes.”"
"351" ""
"352" "“Not a bit, doctor. Stay where you are. I am lost without my Boswell."
"353" "And this promises to be interesting. It would be a pity to miss it.”"
"354" ""
"355" "“But your client—”"
"356" ""
"357" "“Never mind him. I may want your help, and so may he. Here he comes."
"358" "Sit down in that arm-chair, doctor, and give us your best attention.”"
"359" ""
"360" "A slow and heavy step, which had been heard upon the stairs and in the"
"361" "passage, paused immediately outside the door. Then there was a loud and"
"362" "authoritative tap."
"363" ""
"364" "“Come in!” said Holmes."
"365" ""
"366" "[Illustration: “A MAN ENTERED”]"
"367" ""
"368" "A man entered who could hardly have been less than six feet six inches"
"369" "in height, with the chest and limbs of a Hercules. His dress was rich"
"370" "with a richness which would, in England, be looked upon as akin to bad"
"371" "taste. Heavy bands of Astrakhan were slashed across the sleeves and"
"372" "fronts of his double-breasted coat, while the deep blue cloak which"
"373" "was thrown over his shoulders was lined with flame-colored silk, and"
"374" "secured at the neck with a brooch which consisted of a single flaming"
"375" "beryl. Boots which extended half-way up his calves, and which were"
"376" "trimmed at the tops with rich brown fur, completed the impression of"
"377" "barbaric opulence which was suggested by his whole appearance. He"
"378" "carried a broad-brimmed hat in his hand, while he wore across the upper"
"379" "part of his face, extending down past the cheekbones, a black vizard"
"380" "mask, which he had apparently adjusted that very moment, for his hand"
"381" "was still raised to it as he entered. From the lower part of the face"
"382" "he appeared to be a man of strong character, with a thick, hanging"
"383" "lip, and a long, straight chin, suggestive of resolution pushed to the"
"384" "length of obstinacy."
"385" ""
"386" "“You had my note?” he asked, with a deep harsh voice and a strongly"
"387" "marked German accent. “I told you that I would call.” He looked from"
"388" "one to the other of us, as if uncertain which to address."
"389" ""
"390" "“Pray take a seat,” said Holmes. “This is my friend and colleague, Dr."
"391" "Watson, who is occasionally good enough to help me in my cases. Whom"
"392" "have I the honor to address?”"
"393" ""
"394" "“You may address me as the Count Von Kramm, a Bohemian nobleman."
"395" "I understand that this gentleman, your friend, is a man of honor"
"396" "and discretion, whom I may trust with a matter of the most extreme"
"397" "importance. If not, I should much prefer to communicate with you alone.”"
"398" ""
"399" "I rose to go, but Holmes caught me by the wrist and pushed me back into"
"400" "my chair. “It is both, or none,” said he. “You may say before this"
"401" "gentleman anything which you may say to me.”"
"402" ""
"403" "The count shrugged his broad shoulders. “Then I must begin,” said he,"
"404" "“by binding you both to absolute secrecy for two years, at the end of"
"405" "that time the matter will be of no importance. At present it is not too"
"406" "much to say that it is of such weight it may have an influence upon"
"407" "European history.”"
"408" ""
"409" "“I promise,” said Holmes."
"410" ""
"411" "“And I.”"
"412" ""
"413" "“You will excuse this mask,” continued our strange visitor. “The august"
"414" "person who employs me wishes his agent to be unknown to you, and I may"
"415" "confess at once that the title by which I have just called myself is"
"416" "not exactly my own.”"
"417" ""
"418" "“I was aware of it,” said Holmes, dryly."
"419" ""
"420" "“The circumstances are of great delicacy, and every precaution has"
"421" "to be taken to quench what might grow to be an immense scandal and"
"422" "seriously compromise one of the reigning families of Europe. To speak"
"423" "plainly, the matter implicates the great House of Ormstein, hereditary"
"424" "kings of Bohemia.”"
"425" ""
"426" "“I was also aware of that,” murmured Holmes, settling himself down in"
"427" "his arm-chair and closing his eyes."
"428" ""
"429" "Our visitor glanced with some apparent surprise at the languid,"
"430" "lounging figure of the man who had been no doubt depicted to him as"
"431" "the most incisive reasoner and most energetic agent in Europe. Holmes"
"432" "slowly reopened his eyes and looked impatiently at his gigantic client."
"433" ""
"434" "“If your Majesty would condescend to state your case,” he remarked, “I"
"435" "should be better able to advise you.”"
"436" ""
"437" "The man sprang from his chair and paced up and down the room in"
"438" "uncontrollable agitation. Then, with a gesture of desperation, he tore"
"439" "the mask from his face and hurled it upon the ground. “You are right,”"
"440" "he cried; “I am the King. Why should I attempt to conceal it?”"
"441" ""
"442" "“Why, indeed?” murmured Holmes. “Your Majesty had not spoken before"
"443" "I was aware that I was addressing Wilhelm Gottsreich Sigismond von"
"444" "Ormstein, Grand Duke of Cassel-Felstein, and hereditary King of"
"445" "Bohemia.”"
"446" ""
"447" "“But you can understand,” said our strange visitor, sitting down once"
"448" "more and passing his hand over his high, white forehead, “you can"
"449" "understand that I am not accustomed to doing such business in my own"
"450" "person. Yet the matter was so delicate that I could not confide it to"
"451" "an agent without putting myself in his power. I have come _incognito_"
"452" "from Prague for the purpose of consulting you.”"
"453" ""
"454" "“Then, pray consult,” said Holmes, shutting his eyes once more."
"455" ""
"456" "“The facts are briefly these: Some five years ago, during a lengthy"
"457" "visit to Warsaw, I made the acquaintance of the well-known"
"458" "adventuress, Irene Adler. The name is no doubt familiar to you.”"
"459" ""
"460" "“Kindly look her up in my index, doctor,” murmured Holmes, without"
"461" "opening his eyes. For many years he had adopted a system of docketing"
"462" "all paragraphs concerning men and things, so that it was difficult"
"463" "to name a subject or a person on which he could not at once furnish"
"464" "information. In this case I found her biography sandwiched in between"
"465" "that of a Hebrew Rabbi and that of a staff-commander who had written a"
"466" "monograph upon the deep-sea fishes."
"467" ""
"468" "“Let me see!” said Holmes. “Hum! Born in New Jersey in the year"
"469" "1858. Contralto—hum! La Scala, hum! Prima donna Imperial Opera of"
"470" "Warsaw—Yes! Retired from operatic stage—ha! Living in London—quite"
"471" "so! Your Majesty, as I understand, became entangled with this young"
"472" "person, wrote her some compromising letters, and is now desirous of"
"473" "getting those letters back.”"
"474" ""
"475" "“Precisely so. But how—”"
"476" ""
"477" "“Was there a secret marriage?”"
"478" ""
"479" "“None.”"
"480" ""
"481" "“No legal papers or certificates?”"
"482" ""
"483" "“None.”"
"484" ""
"485" "“Then I fail to follow your Majesty. If this young person should"
"486" "produce her letters for blackmailing or other purposes, how is she to"
"487" "prove their authenticity?”"
"488" ""
"489" "“There is the writing.”"
"490" ""
"491" "“Pooh, pooh! Forgery.”"
"492" ""
"493" "“My private note-paper.”"
"494" ""
"495" "“Stolen.”"
"496" ""
"497" "“My own seal.”"
"498" ""
"499" "“Imitated.”"
"500" ""
"501" "“My photograph.”"
"502" ""
"503" "“Bought.”"
"504" ""
"505" "“We were both in the photograph.”"
"506" ""
"507" "“Oh dear! That is very bad! Your Majesty has indeed committed an"
"508" "indiscretion.”"
"509" ""
"510" "“I was mad—insane.”"
"511" ""
"512" "“You have compromised yourself seriously.”"
"513" ""
"514" "“I was only Crown Prince then. I was young. I am but thirty now.”"
"515" ""
"516" "“It must be recovered.”"
"517" ""
"518" "“We have tried and failed.”"
"519" ""
"520" "“Your Majesty must pay. It must be bought.”"
"521" ""
"522" "“She will not sell.”"
"523" ""
"524" "“Stolen, then.”"
"525" ""
"526" "“Five attempts have been made. Twice burglars in my pay ransacked her"
"527" "house. Once we diverted her luggage when she travelled. Twice she has"
"528" "been waylaid. There has been no result.”"
"529" ""
"530" "“No sign of it?”"
"531" ""
"532" "“Absolutely none.”"
"533" ""
"534" "Holmes laughed. “It is quite a pretty little problem,” said he."
"535" ""
"536" "“But a very serious one to me,” returned the King, reproachfully."
"537" ""
"538" "“Very, indeed. And what does she propose to do with the photograph?”"
"539" ""
"540" "“To ruin me.”"
"541" ""
"542" "“But how?”"
"543" ""
"544" "“I am about to be married.”"
"545" ""
"546" "“So I have heard.”"
"547" ""
"548" "“To Clotilde Lothman von Saxe-Meningen, second daughter of the King of"
"549" "Scandinavia. You may know the strict principles of her family. She is"
"550" "herself the very soul of delicacy. A shadow of a doubt as to my conduct"
"551" "would bring the matter to an end.”"
"552" ""
"553" "“And Irene Adler?”"
"554" ""
"555" "“Threatens to send them the photograph. And she will do it. I know that"
"556" "she will do it. You do not know her, but she has a soul of steel. She"
"557" "has the face of the most beautiful of women, and the mind of the most"
"558" "resolute of men. Rather than I should marry another woman, there are"
"559" "no lengths to which she would not go—none.”"
"560" ""
"561" "“You are sure that she has not sent it yet?”"
"562" ""
"563" "“I am sure.”"
"564" ""
"565" "“And why?”"
"566" ""
"567" "“Because she has said that she would send it on the day when the"
"568" "betrothal was publicly proclaimed. That will be next Monday.”"
"569" ""
"570" "“Oh, then, we have three days yet,” said Holmes, with a yawn. “That is"

"574" ""

"576" "Count Von Kramm.”"
"577" ""

"579" ""

"585" ""
"586" "“Absolutely?”"
"587" ""

"590" ""

"592" ""
"593" "The king took a heavy chamois leather bag from under his cloak and laid"

"595" ""

"598" ""

"601" ""

"603" ""

"605" ""

"607" "photograph a cabinet?”"
"608" ""
"609" "“It was.”"
"610" ""
"611" "“Then, good-night, your Majesty, and I trust that we shall soon have"

"616" ""
"617" ""
"618" "II"
"619" ""
"620" "At three o’clock precisely I was at Baker Street, but Holmes had not"
"621" "yet returned. The landlady informed me that he had left the house"
"622" "shortly after eight o’clock in the morning. I sat down beside the"
"623" "fire, however, with the intention of awaiting him, however long he"
"624" "might be. I was already deeply interested in his inquiry, for, though"
"625" "it was surrounded by none of the grim and strange features which"
"626" "were associated with the two crimes which I have already recorded,"
"627" "still, the nature of the case and the exalted station of his client"
"628" "gave it a character of its own. Indeed, apart from the nature of the"
"629" "investigation which my friend had on hand, there was something in his"
"630" "masterly grasp of a situation, and his keen, incisive reasoning, which"
"631" "made it a pleasure to me to study his system of work, and to follow the"
"632" "quick, subtle methods by which he disentangled the most inextricable"
"633" "mysteries. So accustomed was I to his invariable success that the very"
"634" "possibility of his failing had ceased to enter into my head."
"635" ""
"636" "It was close upon four before the door opened, and a drunken-looking"
"637" "groom, ill-kempt and side-whiskered, with an inflamed face and"
"638" "disreputable clothes, walked into the room. Accustomed as I was to"
"639" "my friend’s amazing powers in the use of disguises, I had to look"
"640" "three times before I was certain that it was indeed he. With a nod"
"641" "he vanished into the bedroom, whence he emerged in five minutes"
"642" "tweed-suited and respectable, as of old. Putting his hands into his"
"643" "pockets, he stretched out his legs in front of the fire, and laughed"
"644" "heartily for some minutes."
"645" ""
"646" "“Well, really!” he cried, and then he choked; and laughed again until"
"647" "he was obliged to lie back, limp and helpless, in the chair."
"648" ""
"649" "“What is it?”"
"650" ""
"651" "“It’s quite too funny. I am sure you could never guess how I employed"
"652" "my morning, or what I ended by doing.”"
"653" ""
"654" "“I can’t imagine. I suppose that you have been watching the habits, and"
"655" "perhaps the house, of Miss Irene Adler.”"
"656" ""
"657" "“Quite so; but the sequel was rather unusual. I will tell you, however."
"658" "I left the house a little after eight o’clock this morning, in the"
"659" "character of a groom out of work. There is a wonderful sympathy and"
"660" "freemasonry among horsey men. Be one of them, and you will know all"
"661" "that there is to know. I soon found Briony Lodge. It is a _bijou_"
"662" "villa, with a garden at the back, but built out in front right up to"
"663" "the road, two stories. Chubb lock to the door. Large sitting-room on"
"664" "the right side, well furnished, with long windows almost to the floor,"
"665" "and those preposterous English window fasteners which a child could"
"666" "open. Behind there was nothing remarkable, save that the passage window"
"667" "could be reached from the top of the coach-house. I walked round it"
"668" "and examined it closely from every point of view, but without noting"
"669" "anything else of interest."
"670" ""
"671" "“I then lounged down the street, and found, as I expected, that there"
"672" "was a mews in a lane which runs down by one wall of the garden. I lent"
"673" "the ostlers a hand in rubbing down their horses, and I received in"
"674" "exchange twopence, a glass of half-and-half, two fills of shag tobacco,"
"675" "and as much information as I could desire about Miss Adler, to say"
"676" "nothing of half a dozen other people in the neighborhood in whom I was"
"677" "not in the least interested, but whose biographies I was compelled to"
"678" "listen to.”"
"679" ""
"680" "“And what of Irene Adler?” I asked."
"681" ""
"682" "“Oh, she has turned all the men’s heads down in that part. She"
"683" "is the daintiest thing under a bonnet on this planet. So say the"
"684" "Serpentine-mews, to a man. She lives quietly, sings at concerts, drives"
"685" "out at five every day, and returns at seven sharp for dinner. Seldom"
"686" "goes out at other times, except when she sings. Has only one male"
"687" "visitor, but a good deal of him. He is dark, handsome, and dashing,"
"688" "never calls less than once a day, and often twice. He is a Mr. Godfrey"
"689" "Norton, of the Inner Temple. See the advantages of a cabman as a"
"690" "confidant. They had driven him home a dozen times from Serpentine-mews,"
"691" "and knew all about him. When I had listened to all that they had to"
"692" "tell, I began to walk up and down near Briony Lodge once more, and to"
"693" "think over my plan of campaign."
"694" ""
"695" "“This Godfrey Norton was evidently an important factor in the"
"696" "matter. He was a lawyer. That sounded ominous. What was the relation"
"697" "between them, and what the object of his repeated visits? Was she"
"698" "his client, his friend, or his mistress? If the former, she had"
"699" "probably transferred the photograph to his keeping. If the latter,"
"700" "it was less likely. On the issue of this question depended whether I"
"701" "should continue my work at Briony Lodge, or turn my attention to the"
"702" "gentleman’s chambers in the Temple. It was a delicate point, and it"
"703" "widened the field of my inquiry. I fear that I bore you with these"
"704" "details, but I have to let you see my little difficulties, if you are"
"705" "to understand the situation.”"
"706" ""
"707" "“I am following you closely,” I answered."
"708" ""
"709" "“I was still balancing the matter in my mind, when a hansom cab drove"
"710" "up to Briony Lodge, and a gentleman sprang out. He was a remarkably"
"711" "handsome man, dark, aquiline, and mustached—evidently the man of whom"
"712" "I had heard. He appeared to be in a great hurry, shouted to the cabman"
"713" "to wait, and brushed past the maid who opened the door with the air of"
"714" "a man who was thoroughly at home."
"715" ""
"716" "“He was in the house about half an hour, and I could catch glimpses of"
"717" "him in the windows of the sitting-room, pacing up and down, talking"
"718" "excitedly, and waving his arms. Of her I could see nothing. Presently"
"719" "he emerged, looking even more flurried than before. As he stepped up"
"720" "to the cab, he pulled a gold watch from his pocket and looked at it"
"721" "earnestly. ‘Drive like the devil,’ he shouted, ‘first to Gross &"
"722" "Hankey’s in Regent Street, and then to the church of St. Monica in the"
"723" "Edgware Road. Half a guinea if you do it in twenty minutes!’"
"724" ""
"725" "“Away they went, and I was just wondering whether I should not do"

"727" "coachman with his coat only half-buttoned, and his tie under his ear,"
"728" "while all the tags of his harness were sticking out of the buckles. It"

"731" "with a face that a man might die for."
"732" ""
"733" "“‘The Church of St. Monica, John,’ she cried, ‘and half a sovereign if"
"734" "you reach it in twenty minutes.’"
"735" ""
"736" "“This was quite too good to lose, Watson. I was just balancing whether"
"737" "I should run for it, or whether I should perch behind her landau,"
"738" "when a cab came through the street. The driver looked twice at such a"
"739" "shabby fare; but I jumped in before he could object. ‘The Church of"
"740" "St. Monica,’ said I, ‘and half a sovereign if you reach it in twenty"
"741" "minutes.’ It was twenty-five minutes to twelve, and of course it was"
"742" "clear enough what was in the wind."
"743" ""
"744" "“My cabby drove fast. I don’t think I ever drove faster, but the others"
"745" "were there before us. The cab and the landau with their steaming horses"
"746" "were in front of the door when I arrived. I paid the man and hurried"
"747" "into the church. There was not a soul there save the two whom I had"
"748" "followed and a surpliced clergyman, who seemed to be expostulating with"
"749" "them. They were all three standing in a knot in front of the altar. I"
"750" "lounged up the side aisle like any other idler who has dropped into a"
"751" "church. Suddenly, to my surprise, the three at the altar faced round to"
"752" "me, and Godfrey Norton came running as hard as he could towards me.”"
"753" ""
"754" "“Thank God!” he cried. “You’ll do. Come! Come!”"
"755" ""
"756" "“What then?” I asked."
"757" ""
"758" "“Come, man, come, only three minutes, or it won’t be legal.”"
"759" ""
"760" "“I was half-dragged up to the altar, and, before I knew where I was, I"
"761" "found myself mumbling responses which were whispered in my ear, and"
"762" "vouching for things of which I knew nothing, and generally assisting"
"763" "in the secure tying up of Irene Adler, spinster, to Godfrey Norton,"
"764" "bachelor. It was all done in an instant, and there was the gentleman"
"765" "thanking me on the one side and the lady on the other, while the"

"769" "some informality about their license, that the clergyman absolutely"
"770" "refused to marry them without a witness of some sort, and that my lucky"
"771" "appearance saved the bridegroom from having to sally out into the"
"772" "streets in search of a best man. The bride gave me a sovereign, and I"
"773" "mean to wear it on my watch-chain in memory of the occasion.”"
"774" ""

"776" ""

"786" ""

"852" ""

"854" ""

"856" ""

"859" ""
"860" "He disappeared into his bedroom, and returned in a few minutes in the"
"861" "character of an amiable and simple-minded Nonconformist clergyman. His"
"862" "broad black hat, his baggy trousers, his white tie, his sympathetic"

"866" "seemed to vary with every fresh part that he assumed. The stage lost a"
"867" "fine actor, even as science lost an acute reasoner, when he became a"
"868" "specialist in crime."
"869" ""
"870" "It was a quarter past six when we left Baker Street, and it still"
"871" "wanted ten minutes to the hour when we found ourselves in Serpentine"
"872" "Avenue. It was already dusk, and the lamps were just being lighted as"
"873" "we paced up and down in front of Briony Lodge, waiting for the coming"
"874" "of its occupant. The house was just such as I had pictured it from"
"875" "Sherlock Holmes’s succinct description, but the locality appeared to"
"876" "be less private that I expected. On the contrary, for a small street"
"877" "in a quiet neighborhood, it was remarkably animated. There was a"
"878" "group of shabbily-dressed men smoking and laughing in a corner, a"
"879" "scissors-grinder with his wheel, two guardsmen who were flirting with a"
"880" "nurse-girl, and several well-dressed young men who were lounging up and"
"881" "down with cigars in their mouths."
"882" ""
"883" "“You see,” remarked Holmes, as we paced to and fro in front of the"
"884" "house, “this marriage rather simplifies matters. The photograph becomes"
"885" "a double-edged weapon now. The chances are that she would be as averse"
"886" "to its being seen by Mr. Godfrey Norton, as our client is to its coming"
"887" "to the eyes of his princess. Now the question is, Where are we to find"
"888" "the photograph?”"
"889" ""
"890" "“Where, indeed?”"
"891" ""
"892" "“It is most unlikely that she carries it about with her. It is cabinet"
"893" "size. Too large for easy concealment about a woman’s dress. She knows"
"894" "that the King is capable of having her waylaid and searched. Two"
"895" "attempts of the sort have already been made. We may take it, then, that"
"896" "she does not carry it about with her.”"
"897" ""
"898" "“Where, then?”"
"899" ""
"900" "“Her banker or her lawyer. There is that double possibility. But I am"
"901" "inclined to think neither. Women are naturally secretive, and they"
"902" "like to do their own secreting. Why should she hand it over to any one"
"903" "else? She could trust her own guardianship, but she could not tell"
"904" "what indirect or political influence might be brought to bear upon a"
"905" "business man. Besides, remember that she had resolved to use it within"
"906" "a few days. It must be where she can lay her hands upon it. It must be"
"907" "in her own house.”"
"908" ""
"909" "“But it has twice been burgled.”"
"910" ""
"911" "“Pshaw! They did not know how to look.”"
"912" ""
"913" "“But how will you look?”"
"914" ""
"915" "“I will not look.”"
"916" ""
"917" "“What then?”"
"918" ""
"919" "“I will get her to show me.”"
"920" ""

"922" ""
"923" "“She will not be able to. But I hear the rumble of wheels. It is her"
"924" "carriage. Now carry out my orders to the letter.”"
"925" ""
"926" "As he spoke the gleam of the side-lights of a carriage came round the"
"927" "curve of the avenue. It was a smart little landau which rattled up to"
"928" "the door of Briony Lodge. As it pulled up, one of the loafing men at"
"929" "the corner dashed forward to open the door in the hope of earning a"
"930" "copper, but was elbowed away by another loafer, who had rushed up with"
"931" "the same intention. A fierce quarrel broke out, which was increased by"
"932" "the two guardsmen, who took sides with one of the loungers, and by the"
"933" "scissors-grinder, who was equally hot upon the other side. A blow was"
"934" "struck, and in an instant the lady, who had stepped from her carriage,"
"935" "was the centre of a little knot of flushed and struggling men, who"
"936" "struck savagely at each other with their fists and sticks. Holmes"
"937" "dashed into the crowd to protect the lady; but just as he reached her"
"938" "he gave a cry and dropped to the ground, with the blood running freely"
"939" "down his face. At his fall the guardsmen took to their heels in one"
"940" "direction and the loungers in the other, while a number of better"
"941" "dressed people, who had watched the scuffle without taking part in it,"
"942" "crowded in to help the lady and to attend to the injured man. Irene"
"943" "Adler, as I will still call her, had hurried up the steps; but she"
"944" "stood at the top with her superb figure outlined against the lights of"
"945" "the hall, looking back into the street."
"946" ""
"947" "“Is the poor gentleman much hurt?” she asked."
"948" ""
"949" "“He is dead,” cried several voices."
"950" ""
"951" "“No, no, there’s life in him!” shouted another. “But he’ll be gone"
"952" "before you can get him to hospital.”"
"953" ""
"954" "“He’s a brave fellow,” said a woman. “They would have had the lady’s"
"955" "purse and watch if it hadn’t been for him. They were a gang, and a"
"956" "rough one, too. Ah, he’s breathing now.”"
"957" ""

"959" ""

"962" ""
"963" "Slowly and solemnly he was borne into Briony Lodge and laid out in the"
"964" "principal room, while I still observed the proceedings from my post"
"965" "by the window. The lamps had been lit, but the blinds had not been"
"966" "drawn, so that I could see Holmes as he lay upon the couch. I do not"
"967" "know whether he was seized with compunction at that moment for the part"
"968" "he was playing, but I know that I never felt more heartily ashamed of"
"969" "myself in my life than when I saw the beautiful creature against whom"

"973" "I hardened my heart, and took the smoke-rocket from under my ulster."
"974" "After all, I thought, we are not injuring her. We are but preventing"
"975" "her from injuring another."
"976" ""
"977" "Holmes had sat up upon the couch, and I saw him motion like a man who"
"978" "is in need of air. A maid rushed across and threw open the window. At"
"979" "the same instant I saw him raise his hand, and at the signal I tossed"
"980" "my rocket into the room with a cry of “Fire!” The word was no sooner"

"982" "ill—gentlemen, ostlers, and servant-maids—joined in a general shriek"

"984" "the open window. I caught a glimpse of rushing figures, and a moment"

"986" "alarm. Slipping through the shouting crowd I made my way to the corner"
"987" "of the street, and in ten minutes was rejoiced to find my friend’s arm"
"988" "in mine, and to get away from the scene of uproar. He walked swiftly"
"989" "and in silence for some few minutes, until we had turned down one of"
"990" "the quiet streets which lead towards the Edgware Road."
"991" ""
"992" "“You did it very nicely, doctor,” he remarked. “Nothing could have been"
"993" "better. It is all right.”"
"994" ""
"995" "“You have the photograph?”"
"996" ""

"1002" ""

"1004" ""

"1008" ""

"1010" ""

"1013" "face, and became a piteous spectacle. It is an old trick.”"
"1014" ""
"1015" "“That also I could fathom.”"
"1016" ""
"1017" "“Then they carried me in. She was bound to have me in. What else could"
"1018" "she do? And into her sitting-room, which was the very room which I"
"1019" "suspected. It lay between that and her bedroom, and I was determined"
"1020" "to see which. They laid me on a couch, I motioned for air, they were"
"1021" "compelled to open the window, and you had your chance.”"
"1022" ""
"1023" "“How did that help you?”"
"1024" ""
"1025" "“It was all-important. When a woman thinks that her house is on fire,"
"1026" "her instinct is at once to rush to the thing which she values most. It"
"1027" "is a perfectly overpowering impulse, and I have more than once taken"
"1028" "advantage of it. In the case of the Darlington Substitution Scandal it"
"1029" "was of use to me, and also in the Arnsworth Castle business. A married"
"1030" "woman grabs at her baby; an unmarried one reaches for her jewel-box."
"1031" "Now it was clear to me that our lady of to-day had nothing in the house"

"1033" "secure it. The alarm of fire was admirably done. The smoke and shouting"
"1034" "were enough to shake nerves of steel. She responded beautifully. The"
"1035" "photograph is in a recess behind a sliding panel just above the right"
"1036" "bell-pull. She was there in an instant, and I caught a glimpse of it as"
"1037" "she half-drew it out. When I cried out that it was a false alarm, she"
"1038" "replaced it, glanced at the rocket, rushed from the room, and I have"
"1039" "not seen her since. I rose, and, making my excuses, escaped from the"
"1040" "house. I hesitated whether to attempt to secure the photograph at once;"
"1041" "but the coachman had come in, and as he was watching me narrowly, it"
"1042" "seemed safer to wait. A little over-precipitance may ruin all.”"
"1043" ""
"1044" "“And now?” I asked."
"1045" ""

"1234" "I had called upon my friend, Mr. Sherlock Holmes, one day in the autumn"
"1235" "of last year, and found him in deep conversation with a very stout,"
"1236" "florid-faced, elderly gentleman, with fiery red hair. With an apology"
"1237" "for my intrusion, I was about to withdraw, when Holmes pulled me"
"1238" "abruptly into the room and closed the door behind me."
"1239" ""
"1240" "“You could not possibly have come at a better time, my dear Watson,” he"
"1241" "said, cordially."
"1242" ""
"1243" "“I was afraid that you were engaged.”"
"1244" ""
"1245" "“So I am. Very much so.”"
"1246" ""
"1247" "“Then I can wait in the next room.”"
"1248" ""
"1249" "“Not at all. This gentleman, Mr. Wilson, has been my partner and helper"
"1250" "in many of my most successful cases, and I have no doubt that he will"
"1251" "be of the utmost use to me in yours also.”"
"1252" ""
"1253" "The stout gentleman half-rose from his chair and gave a bob of"
"1254" "greeting, with a quick, little, questioning glance from his small,"
"1255" "fat-encircled eyes."
"1256" ""
"1257" "“Try the settee,” said Holmes, relapsing into his arm-chair and putting"
"1258" "his finger-tips together, as was his custom when in judicial moods. “I"
"1259" "know, my dear Watson, that you share my love of all that is bizarre and"
"1260" "outside the conventions and humdrum routine of every-day life. You have"
"1261" "shown your relish for it by the enthusiasm which has prompted you to"
"1262" "chronicle, and, if you will excuse my saying so, somewhat to embellish"
"1263" "so many of my own little adventures.”"
"1264" ""
"1265" "“Your cases have indeed been of the greatest interest to me,” I"
"1266" "observed."
"1267" ""
"1268" "“You will remember that I remarked the other day, just before we went"
"1269" "into the very simple problem presented by Miss Mary Sutherland, that"
"1270" "for strange effects and extraordinary combinations we must go to"
"1271" "life itself, which is always far more daring than any effort of the"
"1272" "imagination.”"
"1273" ""
"1274" "“A proposition which I took the liberty of doubting.”"
"1275" ""
"1276" "“You did, doctor, but none the less you must come round to my view,"
"1277" "for otherwise I shall keep on piling fact upon fact on you, until your"
"1278" "reason breaks down under them and acknowledges me to be right. Now, Mr."
"1279" "Jabez Wilson here has been good enough to call upon me this morning,"
"1280" "and to begin a narrative which promises to be one of the most singular"
"1281" "which I have listened to for some time. You have heard me remark that"
"1282" "the strangest and most unique things are very often connected not with"
"1283" "the larger but with the smaller crimes, and occasionally, indeed, where"
"1284" "there is room for doubt whether any positive crime has been committed."
"1285" "As far as I have heard it is impossible for me to say whether the"
"1286" "present case is an instance of crime or not, but the course of events"
"1287" "is certainly among the most singular that I have ever listened to."
"1288" "Perhaps, Mr. Wilson, you would have the great kindness to recommence"
"1289" "your narrative. I ask you, not merely because my friend Dr. Watson has"

"1291" "story makes me anxious to have every possible detail from your lips."
"1292" "As a rule, when I have heard some slight indication of the course of"
"1293" "events, I am able to guide myself by the thousands of other similar"
"1294" "cases which occur to my memory. In the present instance I am forced to"
"1295" "admit that the facts are, to the best of my belief, unique.”"
"1296" ""
"1297" "The portly client puffed out his chest with an appearance of some"
"1298" "little pride, and pulled a dirty and wrinkled newspaper from the inside"
"1299" "pocket of his great-coat. As he glanced down the advertisement column,"
"1300" "with his head thrust forward, and the paper flattened out upon his"
"1301" "knee, I took a good look at the man, and endeavored, after the fashion"
"1302" "of my companion, to read the indications which might be presented by"
"1303" "his dress or appearance."
"1304" ""
"1305" "I did not gain very much, however, by my inspection. Our visitor bore"
"1306" "every mark of being an average commonplace British tradesman, obese,"
"1307" "pompous, and slow. He wore rather baggy gray shepherd’s check trousers,"
"1308" "a not over-clean black frock-coat, unbuttoned in the front, and a drab"

"1315" ""

"1878" "from the retired Saxe-Coburg Square presented as great a contrast to"
"1879" "it as the front of a picture does to the back. It was one of the main"
"1880" "arteries which convey the traffic of the city to the north and west."
"1881" "The roadway was blocked with the immense stream of commerce flowing"
"1882" "in a double tide inward and outward, while the foot-paths were black"
"1883" "with the hurrying swarm of pedestrians. It was difficult to realize"
"1884" "as we looked at the line of fine shops and stately business premises"
"1885" "that they really abutted on the other side upon the faded and stagnant"
"1886" "square which we had just quitted."
"1887" ""
"1888" "“Let me see,” said Holmes, standing at the corner, and glancing along"
"1889" "the line, “I should like just to remember the order of the houses here."
"1890" "It is a hobby of mine to have an exact knowledge of London. There is"
"1891" "Mortimer’s, the tobacconist, the little newspaper shop, the Coburg"
"1892" "branch of the City and Suburban Bank, the Vegetarian Restaurant, and"
"1893" "McFarlane’s carriage-building depot. That carries us right on to the"
"1894" "other block. And now, doctor, we’ve done our work, so it’s time we had"
"1895" "some play. A sandwich and a cup of coffee, and then off to violin-land,"
"1896" "where all is sweetness and delicacy and harmony, and there are no"
"1897" "red-headed clients to vex us with their conundrums.”"
"1898" ""
"1899" "My friend was an enthusiastic musician, being himself not only a"
"1900" "very capable performer, but a composer of no ordinary merit. All the"
"1901" "afternoon he sat in the stalls wrapped in the most perfect happiness,"
"1902" "gently waving his long, thin fingers in time to the music, while his"
"1903" "gently smiling face and his languid, dreamy eyes were as unlike those"
"1904" "of Holmes, the sleuth-hound, Holmes the relentless, keen-witted,"
"1905" "ready-handed criminal agent, as it was possible to conceive. In his"
"1906" "singular character the dual nature alternately asserted itself, and"
"1907" "his extreme exactness and astuteness represented, as I have often"
"1908" "thought, the reaction against the poetic and contemplative mood which"
"1909" "occasionally predominated in him. The swing of his nature took him from"
"1910" "extreme languor to devouring energy; and, as I knew well, he was never"
"1911" "so truly formidable as when, for days on end, he had been lounging in"
"1912" "his arm-chair amid his improvisations and his black-letter editions."
"1913" "Then it was that the lust of the chase would suddenly come upon him,"
"1914" "and that his brilliant reasoning power would rise to the level of"
"1915" "intuition, until those who were unacquainted with his methods would"
"1916" "look askance at him as on a man whose knowledge was not that of other"
"1917" "mortals. When I saw him that afternoon so enrapt in the music at St."
"1918" "James’s Hall I felt that an evil time might be coming upon those whom"
"1919" "he had set himself to hunt down."
"1920" ""

"1922" ""
"1923" "“Yes, it would be as well.”"
"1924" ""

"1927" ""

"1929" ""

"1946" "I trust that I am not more dense than my neighbors, but I was always"
"1947" "oppressed with a sense of my own stupidity in my dealings with Sherlock"
"1948" "Holmes. Here I had heard what he had heard, I had seen what he had"
"1949" "seen, and yet from his words it was evident that he saw clearly not"
"1950" "only what had happened, but what was about to happen, while to me the"
"1951" "whole business was still confused and grotesque. As I drove home to"
"1952" "my house in Kensington I thought over it all, from the extraordinary"
"1953" "story of the red-headed copier of the “Encyclopædia” down to the visit"
"1954" "to Saxe-Coburg Square, and the ominous words with which he had parted"
"1955" "from me. What was this nocturnal expedition, and why should I go armed?"
"1956" "Where were we going, and what were we to do? I had the hint from Holmes"
"1957" "that this smooth-faced pawnbroker’s assistant was a formidable man—a"
"1958" "man who might play a deep game. I tried to puzzle it out, but gave it"
"1959" "up in despair, and set the matter aside until night should bring an"
"1960" "explanation."
"1961" ""
"1962" "It was a quarter past nine when I started from home and made my way"
"1963" "across the Park, and so through Oxford Street to Baker Street. Two"
"1964" "hansoms were standing at the door, and, as I entered the passage, I"

"1966" "Holmes in animated conversation with two men, one of whom I recognized"
"1967" "as Peter Jones, the official police agent, while the other was a long,"
"1968" "thin, sad-faced man, with a very shiny hat and oppressively respectable"

"2201" "“You see, Watson,” he explained, in the early hours of the morning,"
"2202" "as we sat over a glass of whiskey-and-soda in Baker Street, “it was"
"2203" "perfectly obvious from the first that the only possible object of this"
"2204" "rather fantastic business of the advertisement of the League, and the"
"2205" "copying of the ‘Encyclopædia,’ must be to get this not over-bright"
"2206" "pawnbroker out of the way for a number of hours every day. It was a"
"2207" "curious way of managing it, but, really, it would be difficult to"
"2208" "suggest a better. The method was no doubt suggested to Clay’s ingenious"
"2209" "mind by the color of his accomplice’s hair. The £4 a week was a lure"
"2210" "which must draw him, and what was it to them, who were playing for"
"2211" "thousands? They put in the advertisement, one rogue has the temporary"
"2212" "office, the other rogue incites the man to apply for it, and together"
"2213" "they manage to secure his absence every morning in the week. From"
"2214" "the time that I heard of the assistant having come for half wages,"
"2215" "it was obvious to me that he had some strong motive for securing the"
"2216" "situation.”"
"2217" ""
"2218" "“But how could you guess what the motive was?”"
"2219" ""

"2221" "vulgar intrigue. That, however, was out of the question. The man’s"
"2222" "business was a small one, and there was nothing in his house which"

"2230" "cellar—something which took many hours a day for months on end. What"
"2231" "could it be, once more? I could think of nothing save that he was"

"2233" ""

"2276" "Adventure III"
"2277" ""
"2278" "A CASE OF IDENTITY"
"2279" ""
"2280" ""
"2281" "“My dear fellow,” said Sherlock Holmes, as we sat on either side"
"2282" "of the fire in his lodgings at Baker Street, “life is infinitely"
"2283" "stranger than anything which the mind of man could invent. We would"
"2284" "not dare to conceive the things which are really mere commonplaces of"
"2285" "existence. If we could fly out of that window hand in hand, hover over"
"2286" "this great city, gently remove the roofs, and peep in at the queer"
"2287" "things which are going on, the strange coincidences, the plannings,"
"2288" "the cross-purposes, the wonderful chains of events, working through"
"2289" "generations, and leading to the most _outré_ results, it would make all"
"2290" "fiction with its conventionalities and foreseen conclusions most stale"
"2291" "and unprofitable.”"
"2292" ""
"2293" "“And yet I am not convinced of it,” I answered. “The cases which come"

"2710" "woman’s sleeve. In a man it is perhaps better first to take the knee"
"2711" "of the trouser. As you observe, this woman had plush upon her sleeves,"
"2712" "which is a most useful material for showing traces. The double line"
"2713" "a little above the wrist, where the type-writist presses against the"
"2714" "table, was beautifully defined. The sewing-machine, of the hand type,"
"2715" "leaves a similar mark, but only on the left arm, and on the side of it"
"2716" "farthest from the thumb, instead of being right across the broadest"
"2717" "part, as this was. I then glanced at her face, and observing the dint"
"2718" "of a pince-nez at either side of her nose, I ventured a remark upon"
"2719" "short sight and type-writing, which seemed to surprise her.”"
"2720" ""
"2721" "“It surprised me.”"
"2722" ""
"2723" "“But, surely, it was very obvious. I was then much surprised and"
"2724" "interested on glancing down to observe that, though the boots which she"
"2725" "was wearing were not unlike each other, they were really odd ones; the"
"2726" "one having a slightly decorated toe-cap, and the other a plain one."
"2727" "One was buttoned only in the two lower buttons out of five, and the"
"2728" "other at the first, third, and fifth. Now, when you see that a young"
"2729" "lady, otherwise neatly dressed, has come away from home with odd boots,"
"2730" "half-buttoned, it is no great deduction to say that she came away in a"
"2731" "hurry.”"
"2732" ""
"2733" "“And what else?” I asked, keenly interested, as I always was, by my"
"2734" "friend’s incisive reasoning."
"2735" ""
"2736" "“I noted, in passing, that she had written a note before leaving home,"
"2737" "but after being fully dressed. You observed that her right glove was"
"2738" "torn at the forefinger, but you did not apparently see that both glove"
"2739" "and finger were stained with violet ink. She had written in a hurry,"
"2740" "and dipped her pen too deep. It must have been this morning, or the"
"2741" "mark would not remain clear upon the finger. All this is amusing,"
"2742" "though rather elementary, but I must go back to business, Watson. Would"
"2743" "you mind reading me the advertised description of Mr. Hosmer Angel?”"
"2744" ""
"2745" "I held the little printed slip to the light. “Missing,” it said, “on"
"2746" "the morning of the 14th, a gentleman named Hosmer Angel. About 5 ft. 7"
"2747" "in. in height; strongly built, sallow complexion, black hair, a little"
"2748" "bald in the centre, bushy, black side-whiskers and mustache; tinted"
"2749" "glasses, slight infirmity of speech. Was dressed, when last seen, in"
"2750" "black frock-coat faced with silk, black waistcoat, gold Albert chain,"
"2751" "and gray Harris tweed trousers, with brown gaiters over elastic-sided"

"2753" "Anybody bringing,” etc., etc."
"2754" ""

"2759" ""

"2761" ""

"2763" "little ‘Hosmer Angel’ at the bottom. There is a date, you see, but no"
"2764" "superscription except Leadenhall Street, which is rather vague. The"
"2765" "point about the signature is very suggestive—in fact, we may call it"
"2766" "conclusive.”"
"2767" ""
"2768" "“Of what?”"
"2769" ""
"2770" "“My dear fellow, is it possible you do not see how strongly it bears"

"2772" ""
"2773" "“I cannot say that I do, unless it were that he wished to be able to"

"2775" ""

"2783" ""

"2798" ""
"2799" "A professional case of great gravity was engaging my own attention at"

"2858" ""

"2911" ""
"2912" "“The man married a woman very much older than himself for her money,”"
"2913" "said he, “and he enjoyed the use of the money of the daughter as long"

"2916" "It was worth an effort to preserve it. The daughter was of a good,"

"2924" "She became restive, insisted upon her rights, and finally announced her"

"2932" "lovers by making love himself.”"
"2933" ""
"2934" "[Illustration: “GLANCING ABOUT HIM LIKE A RAT IN A TRAP”]"
"2935" ""
"2936" "“It was only a joke at first,” groaned our visitor. “We never thought"

"2938" ""

"2962" ""

"2984" ""

"2988" "The case has, in some respects, been not entirely devoid of interest.”"
"2989" ""
"2990" "“I cannot now entirely see all the steps of your reasoning,” I remarked."
"2991" ""
"2992" "“Well, of course it was obvious from the first that this Mr. Hosmer"
"2993" "Angel must have some strong object for his curious conduct, and it was"
"2994" "equally clear that the only man who really profited by the incident,"
"2995" "as far as we could see, was the step-father. Then the fact that the"
"2996" "two men were never together, but that the one always appeared when"
"2997" "the other was away, was suggestive. So were the tinted spectacles and"
"2998" "the curious voice, which both hinted at a disguise, as did the bushy"
"2999" "whiskers. My suspicions were all confirmed by his peculiar action"
"3000" "in type-writing his signature, which, of course, inferred that his"
"3001" "handwriting was so familiar to her that she would recognize even the"
"3002" "smallest sample of it. You see all these isolated facts, together with"
"3003" "many minor ones, all pointed in the same direction.”"
"3004" ""
"3005" "“And how did you verify them?”"
"3006" ""
"3007" "“Having once spotted my man, it was easy to get corroboration. I"
"3008" "knew the firm for which this man worked. Having taken the printed"
"3009" "description, I eliminated everything from it which could be the result"

"3013" "noticed the peculiarities of the type-writer, and I wrote to the man"
"3014" "himself at his business address, asking him if he would come here. As"
"3015" "I expected, his reply was type-written, and revealed the same trivial"
"3016" "but characteristic defects. The same post brought me a letter from"
"3017" "Westhouse & Marbank, of Fenchurch Street, to say that the description"
"3018" "tallied in every respect with that of their employé, James Windibank."
"3019" "_Voila tout!_”"
"3020" ""

"3022" ""

"3031" "Adventure IV"
"3032" ""
"3033" "THE BOSCOMBE VALLEY MYSTERY"
"3034" ""
"3035" ""
"3036" "We were seated at breakfast one morning, my wife and I, when the maid"
"3037" "brought in a telegram. It was from Sherlock Holmes, and ran in this way:"
"3038" ""
"3039" "“Have you a couple of days to spare? Have just been wired for from"
"3040" "the West of England in connection with Boscombe Valley tragedy. Shall"
"3041" "be glad if you will come with me. Air and scenery perfect. Leave"
"3042" "Paddington by the 11.15.”"
"3043" ""
"3044" "“What do you say, dear?” said my wife, looking across at me. “Will you"
"3045" "go?”"
"3046" ""
"3047" "“I really don’t know what to say. I have a fairly long list at present.”"
"3048" ""
"3049" "“Oh, Anstruther would do your work for you. You have been looking a"
"3050" "little pale lately. I think that the change would do you good, and you"
"3051" "are always so interested in Mr. Sherlock Holmes’s cases.”"
"3052" ""
"3053" "“I should be ungrateful if I were not, seeing what I gained through one"
"3054" "of them,” I answered. “But if I am to go, I must pack at once, for I"
"3055" "have only half an hour.”"
"3056" ""
"3057" "My experience of camp life in Afghanistan had at least had the effect"
"3058" "of making me a prompt and ready traveller. My wants were few and"
"3059" "simple, so that in less than the time stated I was in a cab with my"
"3060" "valise, rattling away to Paddington Station. Sherlock Holmes was pacing"
"3061" "up and down the platform, his tall, gaunt figure made even gaunter and"
"3062" "taller by his long gray travelling-cloak and close-fitting cloth cap."
"3063" ""
"3064" "“It is really very good of you to come, Watson,” said he. “It makes a"
"3065" "considerable difference to me, having some one with me on whom I can"
"3066" "thoroughly rely. Local aid is always either worthless or else biassed."
"3067" "If you will keep the two corner seats I shall get the tickets.”"
"3068" ""
"3069" "We had the carriage to ourselves save for an immense litter of papers"
"3070" "which Holmes had brought with him. Among these he rummaged and read,"
"3071" "with intervals of note-taking and of meditation, until we were past"
"3072" "Reading. Then he suddenly rolled them all into a gigantic ball, and"
"3073" "tossed them up onto the rack."
"3074" ""
"3075" "“Have you heard anything of the case?” he asked."
"3076" ""
"3077" "“Not a word. I have not seen a paper for some days.”"
"3078" ""
"3079" "“The London press has not had very full accounts. I have just"
"3080" "been looking through all the recent papers in order to master the"
"3081" "particulars. It seems, from what I gather, to be one of those simple"
"3082" "cases which are so extremely difficult.”"
"3083" ""
"3084" "“That sounds a little paradoxical.”"
"3085" ""
"3086" "“But it is profoundly true. Singularity is almost invariably a clew."
"3087" "The more featureless and commonplace a crime is, the more difficult is"
"3088" "it to bring it home. In this case, however, they have established a"
"3089" "very serious case against the son of the murdered man.”"
"3090" ""
"3091" "“It is a murder, then?”"
"3092" ""
"3093" "“Well, it is conjectured to be so. I shall take nothing for granted"
"3094" "until I have the opportunity of looking personally into it. I will"
"3095" "explain the state of things to you, as far as I have been able to"
"3096" "understand it, in a very few words."
"3097" ""
"3098" "“Boscombe Valley is a country district not very far from Ross, in"
"3099" "Herefordshire. The largest landed proprietor in that part is a Mr. John"
"3100" "Turner, who made his money in Australia, and returned some years ago to"
"3101" "the old country. One of the farms which he held, that of Hatherley, was"
"3102" "let to Mr. Charles McCarthy, who was also an ex-Australian. The men had"
"3103" "known each other in the colonies, so that it was not unnatural that"
"3104" "when they came to settle down they should do so as near each other as"
"3105" "possible. Turner was apparently the richer man, so McCarthy became his"
"3106" "tenant, but still remained, it seems, upon terms of perfect equality,"
"3107" "as they were frequently together. McCarthy had one son, a lad of"
"3108" "eighteen, and Turner had an only daughter of the same age, but neither"
"3109" "of them had wives living. They appear to have avoided the society of"
"3110" "the neighboring English families, and to have led retired lives, though"
"3111" "both the McCarthys were fond of sport, and were frequently seen at"
"3112" "the race-meetings of the neighborhood. McCarthy kept two servants—a"
"3113" "man and a girl. Turner had a considerable household, some half-dozen"
"3114" "at the least. That is as much as I have been able to gather about the"
"3115" "families. Now for the facts."
"3116" ""
"3117" "“On June 3, that is, on Monday last, McCarthy left his house at"
"3118" "Hatherley about three in the afternoon, and walked down to the Boscombe"
"3119" "Pool, which is a small lake formed by the spreading out of the"
"3120" "stream which runs down the Boscombe Valley. He had been out with his"
"3121" "serving-man in the morning at Ross, and he had told the man that he"
"3122" "must hurry, as he had an appointment of importance to keep at three."
"3123" "From that appointment he never came back alive."
"3124" ""
"3125" "“From Hatherley Farm-house to the Boscombe Pool is a quarter of a mile,"
"3126" "and two people saw him as he passed over this ground. One was an old"
"3127" "woman, whose name is not mentioned, and the other was William Crowder,"
"3128" "a game-keeper in the employ of Mr. Turner. Both these witnesses depose"
"3129" "that Mr. McCarthy was walking alone. The game-keeper adds that within"
"3130" "a few minutes of his seeing Mr. McCarthy pass he had seen his son, Mr."
"3131" "James McCarthy, going the same way with a gun under his arm. To the"
"3132" "best of his belief, the father was actually in sight at the time, and"
"3133" "the son was following him. He thought no more of the matter until he"
"3134" "heard in the evening of the tragedy that had occurred."
"3135" ""
"3136" "“The two McCarthys were seen after the time when William Crowder, the"
"3137" "game-keeper, lost sight of them. The Boscombe Pool is thickly-wooded"
"3138" "round, with just a fringe of grass and of reeds round the edge. A girl"
"3139" "of fourteen, Patience Moran, who is the daughter of the lodge-keeper of"
"3140" "the Boscombe Valley estate, was in one of the woods picking flowers."
"3141" "She states that while she was there she saw, at the border of the wood"
"3142" "and close by the lake, Mr. McCarthy and his son, and that they appeared"
"3143" "to be having a violent quarrel. She heard Mr. McCarthy the elder using"
"3144" "very strong language to his son, and she saw the latter raise up"
"3145" "his hand as if to strike his father. She was so frightened by their"
"3146" "violence that she ran away, and told her mother when she reached home"
"3147" "that she had left the two McCarthys quarrelling near Boscombe Pool, and"
"3148" "that she was afraid that they were going to fight. She had hardly said"
"3149" "the words when young Mr. McCarthy came running up to the lodge to say"
"3150" "that he had found his father dead in the wood, and to ask for the help"
"3151" "of the lodge-keeper. He was much excited, without either his gun or his"
"3152" "hat, and his right hand and sleeve were observed to be stained with"
"3153" "fresh blood. On following him they found the dead body stretched out"
"3154" "upon the grass beside the Pool. The head had been beaten in by repeated"
"3155" "blows of some heavy and blunt weapon. The injuries were such as might"
"3156" "very well have been inflicted by the butt-end of his son’s gun, which"
"3157" "was found lying on the grass within a few paces of the body. Under"
"3158" "these circumstances the young man was instantly arrested, and a verdict"
"3159" "of ‘Wilful Murder’ having been returned at the inquest on Tuesday,"
"3160" "he was on Wednesday brought before the magistrates at Ross, who have"
"3161" "referred the case to the next assizes. Those are the main facts of the"
"3162" "case as they came out before the coroner and at the police-court.”"
"3163" ""
"3164" "“I could hardly imagine a more damning case,” I remarked. “If ever"
"3165" "circumstantial evidence pointed to a criminal it does so here.”"
"3166" ""
"3167" "“Circumstantial evidence is a very tricky thing,” answered Holmes,"
"3168" "thoughtfully. “It may seem to point very straight to one thing, but if"
"3169" "you shift your own point of view a little, you may find it pointing"
"3170" "in an equally uncompromising manner to something entirely different."
"3171" "It must be confessed, however, that the case looks exceedingly grave"
"3172" "against the young man, and it is very possible that he is indeed the"
"3173" "culprit. There are several people in the neighborhood, however, and"
"3174" "among them Miss Turner, the daughter of the neighboring land-owner,"
"3175" "who believe in his innocence, and who have retained Lestrade, whom you"
"3176" "may recollect in connection with the Study in Scarlet, to work out the"
"3177" "case in his interest. Lestrade, being rather puzzled, has referred the"
"3178" "case to me, and hence it is that two middle-aged gentlemen are flying"
"3179" "westward at fifty miles an hour, instead of quietly digesting their"
"3180" "breakfasts at home.”"
"3181" ""
"3182" "“I am afraid,” said I, “that the facts are so obvious that you will"
"3183" "find little credit to be gained out of this case.”"
"3184" ""
"3185" "“There is nothing more deceptive than an obvious fact,” he answered,"
"3186" "laughing. “Besides, we may chance to hit upon some other obvious facts"
"3187" "which may have been by no means obvious to Mr. Lestrade. You know me"
"3188" "too well to think that I am boasting when I say that I shall either"
"3189" "confirm or destroy his theory by means which he is quite incapable of"
"3190" "employing, or even of understanding. To take the first example to hand,"
"3191" "I very clearly perceive that in your bedroom the window is upon the"
"3192" "right-hand side, and yet I question whether Mr. Lestrade would have"
"3193" "noted even so self-evident a thing as that.”"
"3194" ""
"3195" "“How on earth—”"
"3196" ""

"3199" "shave by the sunlight; but since your shaving is less and less complete"
"3200" "as we get farther back on the left side, until it becomes positively"

"3263" "“Mr. James McCarthy, the only son of the deceased, was then called, and"

"3544" "back before the blow fell. Still, it might be worth while to call"
"3545" "Holmes’s attention to it. Then there was the peculiar dying reference"
"3546" "to a rat. What could that mean? It could not be delirium. A man dying"
"3547" "from a sudden blow does not commonly become delirious. No, it was more"
"3548" "likely to be an attempt to explain how he met his fate. But what could"
"3549" "it indicate? I cudgelled my brains to find some possible explanation."
"3550" "And then the incident of the gray cloth, seen by young McCarthy. If"
"3551" "that were true, the murderer must have dropped some part of his dress,"
"3552" "presumably his overcoat, in his flight, and must have had the hardihood"
"3553" "to return and to carry it away at the instant when the son was kneeling"
"3554" "with his back turned not a dozen paces off. What a tissue of mysteries"
"3555" "and improbabilities the whole thing was! I did not wonder at Lestrade’s"
"3556" "opinion, and yet I had so much faith in Sherlock Holmes’s insight that"
"3557" "I could not lose hope as long as every fresh fact seemed to strengthen"
"3558" "his conviction of young McCarthy’s innocence."
"3559" ""
"3560" "It was late before Sherlock Holmes returned. He came back alone, for"
"3561" "Lestrade was staying in lodgings in the town."
"3562" ""

"3675" ""
"3676" "[Illustration: “THE MAID SHOWED US THE BOOTS.”]"
"3677" ""
"3678" "Sherlock Holmes was transformed when he was hot upon such a scent"
"3679" "as this. Men who had only known the quiet thinker and logician of"

"3691" "that district, and there were marks of many feet, both upon the path"
"3692" "and amid the short grass which bounded it on either side. Sometimes"

"3697" "actions was directed towards a definite end."
"3698" ""
"3699" "The Boscombe Pool, which is a little reed-girt sheet of water some"
"3700" "fifty yards across, is situated at the boundary between the Hatherley"
"3701" "Farm and the private park of the wealthy Mr. Turner. Above the woods"
"3702" "which lined it upon the farther side we could see the red, jutting"
"3703" "pinnacles which marked the site of the rich land-owner’s dwelling. On"
"3704" "the Hatherley side of the Pool the woods grew very thick, and there was"
"3705" "a narrow belt of sodden grass twenty paces across between the edge of"
"3706" "the trees and the reeds which lined the lake. Lestrade showed us the"
"3707" "exact spot at which the body had been found, and, indeed, so moist was"
"3708" "the ground, that I could plainly see the traces which had been left by"
"3709" "the fall of the stricken man. To Holmes, as I could see by his eager"
"3710" "face and peering eyes, very many other things were to be read upon the"
"3711" "trampled grass. He ran round, like a dog who is picking up a scent, and"
"3712" "then turned upon my companion."
"3713" ""
"3714" "“What did you go into the Pool for?” he asked."
"3715" ""
"3716" "“I fished about with a rake. I thought there might be some weapon or"

"3976" "“It’s as well,” said the old man; “it’s a question whether I shall live"
"3977" "to the Assizes, so it matters little to me, but I should wish to spare"
"3978" "Alice the shock. And now I will make the thing clear to you; it has"
"3979" "been a long time in the acting, but will not take me long to tell."
"3980" ""
"3981" "“You didn’t know this dead man, McCarthy. He was a devil incarnate. I"
"3982" "tell you that. God keep you out of the clutches of such a man as he."
"3983" "His grip has been upon me these twenty years, and he has blasted my"
"3984" "life. I’ll tell you first how I came to be in his power."
"3985" ""
"3986" "“It was in the early sixties at the diggings. I was a young chap then,"
"3987" "hot-blooded and reckless, ready to turn my hand at anything; I got"
"3988" "among bad companions, took to drink, had no luck with my claim, took to"
"3989" "the bush, and in a word became what you would call over here a highway"
"3990" "robber. There were six of us, and we had a wild, free life of it,"
"3991" "sticking up a station from time to time, or stopping the wagons on the"
"3992" "road to the diggings. Black Jack of Ballarat was the name I went under,"
"3993" "and our party is still remembered in the colony as the Ballarat Gang."
"3994" ""
"3995" "“One day a gold convoy came down from Ballarat to Melbourne, and we"
"3996" "lay in wait for it and attacked it. There were six troopers and six of"
"3997" "us, so it was a close thing, but we emptied four of their saddles at"
"3998" "the first volley. Three of our boys were killed, however, before we"
"3999" "got the swag. I put my pistol to the head of the wagon-driver, who was"
"4000" "this very man McCarthy. I wish to the Lord that I had shot him then,"
"4001" "but I spared him, though I saw his wicked little eyes fixed on my face,"
"4002" "as though to remember every feature. We got away with the gold, became"
"4003" "wealthy men, and made our way over to England without being suspected."
"4004" "There I parted from my old pals, and determined to settle down to a"
"4005" "quiet and respectable life. I bought this estate, which chanced to be"
"4006" "in the market, and I set myself to do a little good with my money,"
"4007" "to make up for the way in which I had earned it. I married, too, and"
"4008" "though my wife died young, she left me my dear little Alice. Even when"
"4009" "she was just a baby her wee hand seemed to lead me down the right path"
"4010" "as nothing else had ever done. In a word, I turned over a new leaf, and"
"4011" "did my best to make up for the past. All was going well when McCarthy"
"4012" "laid his grip upon me."
"4013" ""
"4014" "“I had gone up to town about an investment, and I met him in Regent"
"4015" "Street with hardly a coat to his back or a boot to his foot."
"4016" ""
"4017" "“‘Here we are, Jack,’ says he, touching me on the arm; ‘we’ll be as"
"4018" "good as a family to you. There’s two of us, me and my son, and you can"
"4019" "have the keeping of us. If you don’t—it’s a fine, law-abiding country"
"4020" "is England, and there’s always a policeman within hail.’"
"4021" ""
"4022" "“Well, down they came to the West country, there was no shaking them"
"4023" "off, and there they have lived rent free on my best land ever since."
"4024" "There was no rest for me, no peace, no forgetfulness; turn where I"
"4025" "would, there was his cunning, grinning face at my elbow. It grew worse"
"4026" "as Alice grew up, for he soon saw I was more afraid of her knowing my"
"4027" "past than of the police. Whatever he wanted he must have, and whatever"
"4028" "it was I gave him without question, land, money, houses, until at last"
"4029" "he asked a thing which I could not give. He asked for Alice."
"4030" ""
"4031" "“His son, you see, had grown up, and so had my girl, and as I was known"
"4032" "to be in weak health, it seemed a fine stroke to him that his lad"
"4033" "should step into the whole property. But there I was firm. I would not"
"4034" "have his cursed stock mixed with mine; not that I had any dislike to"
"4035" "the lad, but his blood was in him, and that was enough. I stood firm."
"4036" "McCarthy threatened. I braved him to do his worst. We were to meet at"
"4037" "the Pool midway between our houses to talk it over."
"4038" ""
"4039" "“When I went down there I found him talking with his son, so I smoked"
"4040" "a cigar, and waited behind a tree until he should be alone. But as I"
"4041" "listened to his talk all that was black and bitter in me seemed to"
"4042" "come uppermost. He was urging his son to marry my daughter with as"
"4043" "little regard for what she might think as if she were a slut from off"
"4044" "the streets. It drove me mad to think that I and all that I held most"
"4045" "dear should be in the power of such a man as this. Could I not snap the"
"4046" "bond? I was already a dying and a desperate man. Though clear of mind"
"4047" "and fairly strong of limb, I knew that my own fate was sealed. But my"
"4048" "memory and my girl! Both could be saved, if I could but silence that"
"4049" "foul tongue. I did it, Mr. Holmes. I would do it again. Deeply as I"
"4050" "have sinned, I have led a life of martyrdom to atone for it. But that"
"4051" "my girl should be entangled in the same meshes which held me was more"
"4052" "than I could suffer. I struck him down with no more compunction than if"
"4053" "he had been some foul and venomous beast. His cry brought back his son;"
"4054" "but I had gained the cover of the wood, though I was forced to go back"
"4055" "to fetch the cloak which I had dropped in my flight. That is the true"
"4056" "story, gentlemen, of all that occurred.”"
"4057" ""
"4058" "“Well, it is not for me to judge you,” said Holmes, as the old man"
"4059" "signed the statement which had been drawn out. “I pray that we may"
"4060" "never be exposed to such a temptation.”"
"4061" ""
"4062" "“I pray not, sir. And what do you intend to do?”"
"4063" ""
"4064" "“In view of your health, nothing. You are yourself aware that you will"
"4065" "soon have to answer for your deed at a higher court than the Assizes."
"4066" "I will keep your confession, and, if McCarthy is condemned, I shall be"
"4067" "forced to use it. If not, it shall never be seen by mortal eye; and"

"4069" ""
"4070" "“Farewell, then,” said the old man, solemnly. “Your own death-beds,"
"4071" "when they come, will be the easier for the thought of the peace which"
"4072" "you have given to mine.” Tottering and shaking in all his giant frame,"
"4073" "he stumbled slowly from the room."
"4074" ""
"4075" "“God help us!” said Holmes, after a long silence. “Why does fate play"
"4076" "such tricks with poor, helpless worms? I never hear of such a case as"

"4078" "the grace of God, goes Sherlock Holmes.’”"
"4079" ""
"4080" "James McCarthy was acquitted at the Assizes, on the strength of a"
"4081" "number of objections which had been drawn out by Holmes, and submitted"

"4083" "interview, but he is now dead; and there is every prospect that the son"
