"4090" "Adventure V"
"4091" ""
"4092" "THE FIVE ORANGE PIPS"
"4093" ""
"4094" ""
"4095" "When I glance over my notes and records of the Sherlock Holmes cases"
"4096" "between the years ’82 and ’90, I am faced by so many which present"
"4097" "strange and interesting features that it is no easy matter to know"
"4098" "which to choose and which to leave. Some, however, have already gained"
"4099" "publicity through the papers, and others have not offered a field"
"4100" "for those peculiar qualities which my friend possessed in so high a"
"4101" "degree, and which it is the object of these papers to illustrate. Some,"
"4102" "too, have baffled his analytical skill, and would be, as narratives,"
"4103" "beginnings without an ending, while others have been but partially"
"4104" "cleared up, and have their explanations founded rather upon conjecture"
"4105" "and surmise than on that absolute logical proof which was so dear to"
"4106" "him. There is, however, one of these last which was so remarkable in"
"4107" "its details and so startling in its results that I am tempted to give"
"4108" "some account of it, in spite of the fact that there are points in"
"4109" "connection with it which never have been, and probably never will be,"
"4110" "entirely cleared up."
"4111" ""
"4112" "The year ’87 furnished us with a long series of cases of greater"
"4113" "or less interest, of which I retain the records. Among my headings"
"4114" "under this one twelve months I find an account of the adventure of"
"4115" "the Paradol Chamber, of the Amateur Mendicant Society, who held a"
"4116" "luxurious club in the lower vault of a furniture warehouse, of the"
"4117" "facts connected with the loss of the British bark _Sophy Anderson_, of"
"4118" "the singular adventures of the Grice Patersons in the island of Uffa,"
"4119" "and finally of the Camberwell poisoning case. In the latter, as may"
"4120" "be remembered, Sherlock Holmes was able, by winding up the dead man’s"
"4121" "watch, to prove that it had been wound up two hours before, and that"
"4122" "therefore the deceased had gone to bed within that time—a deduction"
"4123" "which was of the greatest importance in clearing up the case. All these"
"4124" "I may sketch out at some future date, but none of them present such"
"4125" "singular features as the strange train of circumstances which I have"
"4126" "now taken up my pen to describe."
"4127" ""
"4128" "It was in the latter days of September, and the equinoctial gales had"
"4129" "set in with exceptional violence. All day the wind had screamed and the"
"4130" "rain had beaten against the windows, so that even here in the heart"
"4131" "of great, hand-made London we were forced to raise our minds for the"
"4132" "instant from the routine of life, and to recognize the presence of"
"4133" "those great elemental forces which shriek at mankind through the bars"
"4134" "of his civilization, like untamed beasts in a cage. As evening drew in,"
"4135" "the storm grew higher and louder, and the wind cried and sobbed like a"
"4136" "child in the chimney. Sherlock Holmes sat moodily at one side of the"
"4137" "fireplace cross-indexing his records of crime, while I at the other was"
"4138" "deep in one of Clark Russell’s fine sea-stories, until the howl of the"
"4139" "gale from without seemed to blend with the text, and the splash of the"
"4140" "rain to lengthen out into the long swash of the sea waves. My wife was"
"4141" "on a visit to her mother’s, and for a few days I was a dweller once"
"4142" "more in my old quarters at Baker Street."
"4143" ""
"4144" "“Why,” said I, glancing up at my companion, “that was surely the bell."
"4145" "Who could come to-night? Some friend of yours, perhaps?”"
"4146" ""
"4147" "“Except yourself I have none,” he answered. “I do not encourage"
"4148" "visitors.”"
"4149" ""
"4150" "“A client, then?”"
"4151" ""
"4152" "“If so, it is a serious case. Nothing less would bring a man out on"
"4153" "such a day and at such an hour. But I take it that it is more likely to"
"4154" "be some crony of the landlady’s.”"
"4155" ""
"4156" "Sherlock Holmes was wrong in his conjecture, however, for there came"
"4157" "a step in the passage and a tapping at the door. He stretched out his"
"4158" "long arm to turn the lamp away from himself and towards the vacant"
"4159" "chair upon which a new-comer must sit. “Come in!” said he."
"4160" ""
"4161" "The man who entered was young, some two-and-twenty at the outside,"
"4162" "well-groomed and trimly clad, with something of refinement and delicacy"
"4163" "in his bearing. The steaming umbrella which he held in his hand, and"
"4164" "his long shining waterproof told of the fierce weather through which he"
"4165" "had come. He looked about him anxiously in the glare of the lamp, and"
"4166" "I could see that his face was pale and his eyes heavy, like those of a"
"4167" "man who is weighed down with some great anxiety."
"4168" ""
"4169" "“I owe you an apology,” he said, raising his golden _pince-nez_ to his"
"4170" "eyes. “I trust that I am not intruding. I fear that I have brought some"
"4171" "traces of the storm and rain into your snug chamber.”"
"4172" ""
"4173" "“Give me your coat and umbrella,” said Holmes. “They may rest here"
"4174" "on the hook, and will be dry presently. You have come up from the"
"4175" "south-west, I see.”"
"4176" ""
"4177" "“Yes, from Horsham.”"
"4178" ""
"4179" "“That clay and chalk mixture which I see upon your toe-caps is quite"
"4180" "distinctive.”"
"4181" ""
"4182" "“I have come for advice.”"
"4183" ""
"4184" "“That is easily got.”"
"4185" ""
"4186" "“And help.”"
"4187" ""
"4188" "“That is not always so easy.”"
"4189" ""
"4190" "“I have heard of you, Mr. Holmes. I heard from Major Prendergast how"
"4191" "you saved him in the Tankerville Club Scandal.”"
"4192" ""
"4193" "“Ah, of course. He was wrongfully accused of cheating at cards.”"
"4194" ""
"4195" "“He said that you could solve anything.”"
"4196" ""
"4197" "“He said too much.”"
"4198" ""
"4199" "“That you are never beaten.”"
"4200" ""
"4201" "“I have been beaten four times—three times by men, and once by a"
"4202" "woman.”"
"4203" ""
"4204" "“But what is that compared with the number of your successes?”"
"4205" ""
"4206" "“It is true that I have been generally successful.”"
"4207" ""
"4208" "“Then you may be so with me.”"
"4209" ""
"4210" "“I beg that you will draw your chair up to the fire, and favor me with"

"4212" ""
"4213" "“It is no ordinary one.”"
"4214" ""
"4215" "“None of those which come to me are. I am the last court of appeal.”"
"4216" ""

"4221" "“You fill me with interest,” said Holmes. “Pray give us the essential"

"4224" ""
"4225" "The young man pulled his chair up, and pushed his wet feet out towards"
"4226" "the blaze."
"4227" ""
"4228" "“My name,” said he, “is John Openshaw, but my own affairs have, as far"
"4229" "as I can understand it, little to do with this awful business. It is an"
"4230" "hereditary matter; so in order to give you an idea of the facts, I must"

"4232" ""
"4233" "“You must know that my grandfather had two sons—my uncle Elias and"
"4234" "my father Joseph. My father had a small factory at Coventry, which"
"4235" "he enlarged at the time of the invention of bicycling. He was the"
"4236" "patentee of the Openshaw unbreakable tire, and his business met with"
"4237" "such success that he was able to sell it, and to retire upon a handsome"
"4238" "competence."
"4239" ""
"4240" "“My uncle Elias emigrated to America when he was a young man, and"
"4241" "became a planter in Florida, where he was reported to have done"
"4242" "very well. At the time of the war he fought in Jackson’s army, and"
"4243" "afterwards under Hood, where he rose to be a colonel. When Lee laid"
"4244" "down his arms my uncle returned to his plantation, where he remained"
"4245" "for three or four years. About 1869 or 1870 he came back to Europe,"
"4246" "and took a small estate in Sussex, near Horsham. He had made a very"
"4247" "considerable fortune in the States, and his reason for leaving them was"
"4248" "his aversion to the negroes, and his dislike of the Republican policy"
"4249" "in extending the franchise to them. He was a singular man, fierce and"
"4250" "quick-tempered, very foul-mouthed when he was angry, and of a most"
"4251" "retiring disposition. During all the years that he lived at Horsham I"
"4252" "doubt if ever he set foot in the town. He had a garden and two or three"
"4253" "fields round his house, and there he would take his exercise, though"
"4254" "very often for weeks on end he would never leave his room. He drank"
"4255" "a great deal of brandy, and smoked very heavily, but he would see no"
"4256" "society, and did not want any friends, not even his own brother."
"4257" ""
"4258" "“He didn’t mind me, in fact, he took a fancy to me, for at the time"
"4259" "when he saw me first I was a youngster of twelve or so. This would be"
"4260" "in the year 1878, after he had been eight or nine years in England. He"
"4261" "begged my father to let me live with him, and he was very kind to me"
"4262" "in his way. When he was sober he used to be fond of playing backgammon"
"4263" "and draughts with me, and he would make me his representative both with"
"4264" "the servants and with the tradespeople, so that by the time that I was"
"4265" "sixteen I was quite master of the house. I kept all the keys, and could"
"4266" "go where I liked and do what I liked, so long as I did not disturb him"
"4267" "in his privacy. There was one singular exception, however, for he had"
"4268" "a single room, a lumber-room up among the attics, which was invariably"
"4269" "locked, and which he would never permit either me or anyone else to"
"4270" "enter. With a boy’s curiosity I have peeped through the key-hole, but"
"4271" "I was never able to see more than such a collection of old trunks and"
"4272" "bundles as would be expected in such a room."
"4273" ""
"4274" "“One day—it was in March, 1883—a letter with a foreign stamp lay"
"4275" "upon the table in front of the Colonel’s plate. It was not a common"
"4276" "thing for him to receive letters, for his bills were all paid in"
"4277" "ready money, and he had no friends of any sort. ‘From India!’ said he,"
"4278" "as he took it up, ‘Pondicherry postmark! What can this be?’ Opening"
"4279" "it hurriedly, out there jumped five little dried orange pips, which"
"4280" "pattered down upon his plate. I began to laugh at this, but the laugh"
"4281" "was struck from my lips at the sight of his face. His lip had fallen,"
"4282" "his eyes were protruding, his skin the color of putty, and he glared at"
"4283" "the envelope which he still held in his trembling hand. ‘K. K. K.!’ he"
"4284" "shrieked, and then, ‘My God, my God, my sins have overtaken me!’"
"4285" ""
"4286" "“‘What is it, uncle?’ I cried."
"4287" ""
"4288" "“‘Death,’ said he, and rising from the table he retired to his room,"
"4289" "leaving me palpitating with horror. I took up the envelope, and saw"
"4290" "scrawled in red ink upon the inner flap, just above the gum, the letter"

"4292" "pips. What could be the reason of his overpowering terror? I left the"

"4296" ""
"4297" "“‘They may do what they like, but I’ll checkmate them still,’ said he,"
"4298" "with an oath. ‘Tell Mary that I shall want a fire in my room to-day,"
"4299" "and send down to Fordham, the Horsham lawyer.’"
"4300" ""
"4301" "“I did as he ordered, and when the lawyer arrived I was asked to step"
"4302" "up to the room. The fire was burning brightly, and in the grate there"
"4303" "was a mass of black, fluffy ashes, as of burned paper, while the brass"
"4304" "box stood open and empty beside it. As I glanced at the box I noticed,"
"4305" "with a start, that upon the lid were printed the treble K which I had"

"4307" ""
"4308" "“‘I wish you, John,’ said my uncle, ‘to witness my will. I leave"
"4309" "my estate, with all its advantages and all its disadvantages to my"
"4310" "brother, your father, whence it will, no doubt, descend to you. If you"
"4311" "can enjoy it in peace, well and good! If you find you cannot, take my"
"4312" "advice, my boy, and leave it to your deadliest enemy. I am sorry to"
"4313" "give you such a two-edged thing, but I can’t say what turn things are"
"4314" "going to take. Kindly sign the paper where Mr. Fordham shows you.’"
"4315" ""
"4316" "“I signed the paper as directed, and the lawyer took it away with him."
"4317" "The singular incident made, as you may think, the deepest impression"
"4318" "upon me, and I pondered over it, and turned it every way in my mind"
"4319" "without being able to make anything of it. Yet I could not shake off"
"4320" "the vague feeling of dread which it left behind though the sensation"
"4321" "grew less keen as the weeks passed, and nothing happened to disturb"
"4322" "the usual routine of our lives. I could see a change in my uncle,"
"4323" "however. He drank more than ever, and he was less inclined for any"
"4324" "sort of society. Most of his time he would spend in his room, with the"
"4325" "door locked upon the inside, but sometimes he would emerge in a sort"
"4326" "of drunken frenzy, and would burst out of the house and tear about the"
"4327" "garden with a revolver in his hand, screaming out that he was afraid"

"4329" "by man or devil. When these hot fits were over, however, he would rush"

"4334" ""
"4335" "“Well, to come to an end of the matter, Mr. Holmes, and not to abuse"
"4336" "your patience, there came a night when he made one of those drunken"
"4337" "sallies from which he never came back. We found him, when we went to"

"4351" ""
"4352" "“The latter arrived on March 10, 1883. His death was seven weeks later,"
"4353" "upon the night of May 2d.”"
"4354" ""
"4355" "“Thank you. Pray proceed.”"
"4356" ""
"4357" "“When my father took over the Horsham property, he, at my request, made"
"4358" "a careful examination of the attic, which had been always locked up. We"

"4372" ""
"4373" "“Well, it was the beginning of ’84 when my father came to live at"

"4809" "gang. That he should come to me for help, and that I should send him"
"4810" "away to his death—!” He sprang from his chair and paced about the room"

"4929" "Adventure VI"
"4930" ""
"4931" "THE MAN WITH THE TWISTED LIP"
"4932" ""
"4933" ""
"4934" "Isa Whitney, brother of the late Elias Whitney, D.D., Principal of the"
"4935" "Theological College of St. George’s, was much addicted to opium. The"
"4936" "habit grew upon him, as I understand, from some foolish freak when he"
"4937" "was at college; for having read De Quincey’s description of his dreams"
"4938" "and sensations, he had drenched his tobacco with laudanum in an attempt"
"4939" "to produce the same effects. He found, as so many more have done, that"
"4940" "the practice is easier to attain than to get rid of, and for many years"
"4941" "he continued to be a slave to the drug, an object of mingled horror"
"4942" "and pity to his friends and relatives. I can see him now, with yellow,"
"4943" "pasty face, drooping lids, and pin-point pupils, all huddled in a"
"4944" "chair, the wreck and ruin of a noble man."
"4945" ""
"4946" "One night—it was in June, ’89—there came a ring to my bell, about the"
"4947" "hour when a man gives his first yawn and glances at the clock. I sat up"
"4948" "in my chair, and my wife laid her needle-work down in her lap and made"
"4949" "a little face of disappointment."
"4950" ""
"4951" "“A patient!” said she. “You’ll have to go out.”"
"4952" ""
"4953" "I groaned, for I was newly come back from a weary day."
"4954" ""
"4955" "We heard the door open, a few hurried words, and then quick steps"
"4956" "upon the linoleum. Our own door flew open, and a lady, clad in some"
"4957" "dark-colored stuff, with a black veil, entered the room."
"4958" ""
"4959" "“You will excuse my calling so late,” she began, and then, suddenly"
"4960" "losing her self-control, she ran forward, threw her arms about my"
"4961" "wife’s neck, and sobbed upon her shoulder. “Oh, I’m in such trouble!”"
"4962" "she cried; “I do so want a little help.”"
"4963" ""
"4964" "“Why,” said my wife, pulling up her veil, “it is Kate Whitney. How you"
"4965" "startled me, Kate! I had not an idea who you were when you came in.”"
"4966" ""
"4967" "“I didn’t know what to do, so I came straight to you.” That was always"
"4968" "the way. Folk who were in grief came to my wife like birds to a"
"4969" "light-house."
"4970" ""
"4971" "“It was very sweet of you to come. Now, you must have some wine and"
"4972" "water, and sit here comfortably and tell us all about it. Or should you"
"4973" "rather that I sent James off to bed?”"
"4974" ""
"4975" "“Oh, no, no! I want the Doctor’s advice and help, too. It’s about Isa."
"4976" "He has not been home for two days. I am so frightened about him!”"
"4977" ""
"4978" "It was not the first time that she had spoken to us of her husband’s"
"4979" "trouble, to me as a doctor, to my wife as an old friend and school"
"4980" "companion. We soothed and comforted her by such words as we could find."
"4981" "Did she know where her husband was? Was it possible that we could bring"
"4982" "him back to her?"
"4983" ""
"4984" "It seemed that it was. She had the surest information that of late he"
"4985" "had, when the fit was on him, made use of an opium den in the farthest"
"4986" "east of the city. Hitherto his orgies had always been confined to one"
"4987" "day, and he had come back, twitching and shattered, in the evening."
"4988" "But now the spell had been upon him eight-and-forty hours, and he lay"
"4989" "there, doubtless among the dregs of the docks, breathing in the poison"
"4990" "or sleeping off the effects. There he was to be found, she was sure of"
"4991" "it, at the “Bar of Gold,” in Upper Swandam Lane. But what was she to"
"4992" "do? How could she, a young and timid woman, make her way into such a"
"4993" "place, and pluck her husband out from among the ruffians who surrounded"
"4994" "him?"
"4995" ""
"4996" "There was the case, and of course there was but one way out of it."
"4997" "Might I not escort her to this place? And then, as a second thought,"
"4998" "why should she come at all? I was Isa Whitney’s medical adviser, and"
"4999" "as such I had influence over him. I could manage it better if I were"
"5000" "alone. I promised her on my word that I would send him home in a"
"5001" "cab within two hours if he were indeed at the address which she had"
"5002" "given me. And so in ten minutes I had left my arm-chair and cheery"
"5003" "sitting-room behind me, and was speeding eastward in a hansom on a"
"5004" "strange errand, as it seemed to me at the time, though the future only"
"5005" "could show how strange it was to be."
"5006" ""
"5007" "But there was no great difficulty in the first stage of my adventure."
"5008" "Upper Swandam Lane is a vile alley lurking behind the high wharves"
"5009" "which line the north side of the river to the east of London Bridge."
"5010" "Between a slop-shop and a gin-shop, approached by a steep flight of"
"5011" "steps leading down to a black gap like the mouth of a cave, I found the"
"5012" "den of which I was in search. Ordering my cab to wait, I passed down"
"5013" "the steps, worn hollow in the centre by the ceaseless tread of drunken"
"5014" "feet, and by the light of a flickering oil-lamp above the door I found"
"5015" "the latch, and made my way into a long, low room, thick and heavy"
"5016" "with the brown opium smoke, and terraced with wooden berths, like the"
"5017" "forecastle of an emigrant ship."
"5018" ""
"5019" "Through the gloom one could dimly catch a glimpse of bodies lying in"
"5020" "strange fantastic poses, bowed shoulders, bent knees, heads thrown back"
"5021" "and chins pointing upward, with here and there a dark, lack-lustre eye"
"5022" "turned upon the new-comer. Out of the black shadows there glimmered"
"5023" "little red circles of light, now bright, now faint, as the burning"
"5024" "poison waxed or waned in the bowls of the metal pipes. The most lay"
"5025" "silent, but some muttered to themselves, and others talked together in"
"5026" "a strange, low, monotonous voice, their conversation coming in gushes,"
"5027" "and then suddenly tailing off into silence, each mumbling out his own"
"5028" "thoughts, and paying little heed to the words of his neighbor. At the"
"5029" "farther end was a small brazier of burning charcoal, beside which on a"
"5030" "three-legged wooden stool there sat a tall, thin old man, with his jaw"
"5031" "resting upon his two fists, and his elbows upon his knees, staring into"
"5032" "the fire."
"5033" ""
"5034" "As I entered, a sallow Malay attendant had hurried up with a pipe for"

"5036" ""

"5208" ""
"5209" "“Some years ago—to be definite, in May, 1884—there came to Lee a"
"5210" "gentleman, Neville St. Clair by name, who appeared to have plenty"
"5211" "of money. He took a large villa, laid out the grounds very nicely,"
"5212" "and lived generally in good style. By degrees he made friends in the"
"5213" "neighborhood, and in 1887 he married the daughter of a local brewer, by"
"5214" "whom he now has two children. He had no occupation, but was interested"
"5215" "in several companies, and went into town as a rule in the morning,"
"5216" "returning by the 5.14 from Cannon Street every night. Mr. St. Clair is"
"5217" "now thirty-seven years of age, is a man of temperate habits, a good"
"5218" "husband, a very affectionate father, and a man who is popular with all"
"5219" "who know him. I may add that his whole debts at the present moment,"
"5220" "as far as we have been able to ascertain, amount to £88 10_s._, while"
"5221" "he has £220 standing to his credit in the Capital and Counties Bank."
"5222" "There is no reason, therefore, to think that money troubles have been"
"5223" "weighing upon his mind."
"5224" ""
"5225" "“Last Monday Mr. Neville St. Clair went into town rather earlier"
"5226" "than usual, remarking before he started that he had two important"
"5227" "commissions to perform, and that he would bring his little boy home a"
"5228" "box of bricks. Now, by the merest chance, his wife received a telegram"
"5229" "upon this same Monday, very shortly after his departure, to the effect"
"5230" "that a small parcel of considerable value which she had been expecting"
"5231" "was waiting for her at the offices of the Aberdeen Shipping Company."
"5232" "Now, if you are well up in your London, you will know that the offices"
"5233" "of the company is in Fresno Street, which branches out of Upper Swandam"

"5242" "“If you remember, Monday was an exceedingly hot day, and Mrs. St."
"5243" "Clair walked slowly, glancing about in the hope of seeing a cab, as"

"5280" ""
"5281" "“This discovery, and the evident confusion which the cripple showed,"

"5284" "The front room was plainly furnished as a sitting-room, and led into a"
"5285" "small bedroom, which looked out upon the back of one of the wharves."
"5286" "Between the wharf and the bedroom window is a narrow strip, which is"
"5287" "dry at low tide, but is covered at high tide with at least four and"
"5288" "a half feet of water. The bedroom window was a broad one, and opened"
"5289" "from below. On examination traces of blood were to be seen upon the"

"5293" "his coat. His boots, his socks, his hat, and his watch—all were there."
"5294" "There were no signs of violence upon any of these garments, and there"
"5295" "were no other traces of Mr. Neville St. Clair. Out of the window he"
"5296" "must apparently have gone, for no other exit could be discovered, and"
"5297" "the ominous blood-stains upon the sill gave little promise that he"
"5298" "could save himself by swimming, for the tide was at its very highest at"
"5299" "the moment of the tragedy."
"5300" ""

"5673" "ounce of shag tobacco and a box of matches laid out in front of him."
"5674" "In the dim light of the lamp I saw him sitting there, an old briar"
"5675" "pipe between his lips, his eyes fixed vacantly upon the corner of the"
"5676" "ceiling, the blue smoke curling up from him, silent, motionless, with"
"5677" "the light shining upon his strong-set aquiline features. So he sat as I"
"5678" "dropped off to sleep, and so he sat when a sudden ejaculation caused me"

"5680" "pipe was still between his lips, the smoke still curled upward, and the"
"5681" "room was full of a dense tobacco haze, but nothing remained of the heap"
"5682" "of shag which I had seen upon the previous night."
"5683" ""
"5684" "“Awake, Watson?” he asked."
"5685" ""
"5686" "“Yes.”"
"5687" ""

"5689" ""
"5690" "“Certainly.”"
"5691" ""

"5696" ""

"5864" "“You are the first who have ever heard my story. My father was"
"5865" "a school-master in Chesterfield, where I received an excellent"
"5866" "education. I travelled in my youth, took to the stage, and finally"

"5868" "wished to have a series of articles upon begging in the metropolis,"
"5869" "and I volunteered to supply them. There was the point from which all"
"5870" "my adventures started. It was only by trying begging as an amateur"
"5871" "that I could get the facts upon which to base my articles. When an"
"5872" "actor I had, of course, learned all the secrets of making up, and had"
"5873" "been famous in the greenroom for my skill. I took advantage now of"
"5874" "my attainments. I painted my face, and to make myself as pitiable as"
"5875" "possible I made a good scar and fixed one side of my lip in a twist"
"5876" "by the aid of a small slip of flesh-colored plaster. Then with a red"
"5877" "head of hair, and an appropriate dress, I took my station in the"

"5879" "beggar. For seven hours I plied my trade, and when I returned home in"
"5880" "the evening I found, to my surprise, that I had received no less than"
"5881" "26_s._ 4_d._"
"5882" ""
"5883" "“I wrote my articles, and thought little more of the matter until, some"
"5884" "time later, I backed a bill for a friend, and had a writ served upon"
"5885" "me for £25. I was at my wits’ end where to get the money, but a sudden"

"5887" "for a holiday from my employers, and spent the time in begging in the"
"5888" "city under my disguise. In ten days I had the money, and had paid the"
"5889" "debt."
"5890" ""
"5891" "“Well, you can imagine how hard it was to settle down to arduous"
"5892" "work at £2 a week, when I knew that I could earn as much in a day by"
"5893" "smearing my face with a little paint, laying my cap on the ground, and"
"5894" "sitting still. It was a long fight between my pride and the money,"
"5895" "but the dollars won at last, and I threw up reporting, and sat day"

"5900" "and in the evenings transform myself into a well-dressed man about"
"5901" "town. This fellow, a Lascar, was well paid by me for his rooms, so that"
"5902" "I knew that my secret was safe in his possession."
"5903" ""
"5904" "“Well, very soon I found that I was saving considerable sums of money."
"5905" "I do not mean that any beggar in the streets of London could earn £700"
"5906" "a year—which is less than my average takings—but I had exceptional"
"5907" "advantages in my power of making up, and also in a facility of"
"5908" "repartee, which improved by practice, and made me quite a recognized"
"5909" "character in the city. All day a stream of pennies, varied by silver,"
"5910" "poured in upon me, and it was a very bad day in which I failed to take"
"5911" "£2."
"5912" ""
"5913" "“As I grew richer I grew more ambitious, took a house in the country,"
"5914" "and eventually married, without any one having a suspicion as to my"

"5916" "little knew what."
"5917" ""
"5918" "“Last Monday I had finished for the day, and was dressing in my room"
"5919" "above the opium den, when I looked out of my window, and saw, to my"

"5925" "my clothes, pulled on those of a beggar, and put on my pigments and"
"5926" "wig. Even a wife’s eyes could not pierce so complete a disguise. But"
"5927" "then it occurred to me that there might be a search in the room, and"
"5928" "that the clothes might betray me. I threw open the window, reopening"
"5929" "by my violence a small cut which I had inflicted upon myself in the"
"5930" "bedroom that morning. Then I seized my coat, which was weighted by"
"5931" "the coppers which I had just transferred to it from the leather bag"
"5932" "in which I carried my takings. I hurled it out of the window, and it"
"5933" "disappeared into the Thames. The other clothes would have followed, but"
"5934" "at that moment there was a rush of constables up the stair, and a few"

"5938" ""
"5939" "“I do not know that there is anything else for me to explain. I was"

"5944" "scrawl, telling her that she had no cause to fear.”"
"5945" ""

"5947" ""

"5954" ""

"5957" ""
"5958" "“Many times; but what was a fine to me?”"
"5959" ""

"5976" ""
"5977" "Adventure VII"
"5978" ""
"5979" "THE ADVENTURE OF THE BLUE CARBUNCLE"
"5980" ""
"5981" ""
"5982" "I had called upon my friend Sherlock Holmes upon the second morning"
"5983" "after Christmas, with the intention of wishing him the compliments of"
"5984" "the season. He was lounging upon the sofa in a purple dressing-gown,"
"5985" "a pipe-rack within his reach upon the right, and a pile of crumpled"
"5986" "morning papers, evidently newly studied, near at hand. Beside the couch"
"5987" "was a wooden chair, and on the angle of the back hung a very seedy"
"5988" "and disreputable hard-felt hat, much the worse for wear, and cracked"
"5989" "in several places. A lens and a forceps lying upon the seat of the"
"5990" "chair suggested that the hat had been suspended in this manner for the"
"5991" "purpose of examination."
"5992" ""
"5993" "“You are engaged,” said I; “perhaps I interrupt you.”"
"5994" ""
"5995" "“Not at all. I am glad to have a friend with whom I can discuss my"
"5996" "results. The matter is a perfectly trivial one” (he jerked his thumb in"
"5997" "the direction of the old hat), “but there are points in connection with"
"5998" "it which are not entirely devoid of interest and even of instruction.”"
"5999" ""
"6000" "I seated myself in his arm-chair and warmed my hands before his"
"6001" "crackling fire, for a sharp frost had set in, and the windows were"
"6002" "thick with the ice crystals. “I suppose,” I remarked, “that, homely as"
"6003" "it looks, this thing has some deadly story linked on to it—that it is"
"6004" "the clew which will guide you in the solution of some mystery and the"
"6005" "punishment of some crime.”"
"6006" ""
"6007" "“No, no. No crime,” said Sherlock Holmes, laughing. “Only one of"
"6008" "those whimsical little incidents which will happen when you have"
"6009" "four million human beings all jostling each other within the space of"
"6010" "a few square miles. Amid the action and reaction of so dense a swarm"
"6011" "of humanity, every possible combination of events may be expected to"
"6012" "take place, and many a little problem will be presented which may"
"6013" "be striking and bizarre without being criminal. We have already had"
"6014" "experience of such.”"
"6015" ""
"6016" "“So much so,” I remarked, “that of the last six cases which I have"
"6017" "added to my notes, three have been entirely free of any legal crime.”"
"6018" ""
"6019" "“Precisely. You allude to my attempt to recover the Irene Adler papers,"
"6020" "to the singular case of Miss Mary Sutherland, and to the adventure of"
"6021" "the man with the twisted lip. Well, I have no doubt that this small"
"6022" "matter will fall into the same innocent category. You know Peterson,"
"6023" "the commissionaire?”"
"6024" ""
"6025" "“Yes.”"
"6026" ""
"6027" "“It is to him that this trophy belongs.”"
"6028" ""
"6029" "“It is his hat.”"
"6030" ""
"6031" "“No, no; he found it. Its owner is unknown. I beg that you will look"
"6032" "upon it, not as a battered billycock, but as an intellectual problem."
"6033" "And, first, as to how it came here. It arrived upon Christmas morning,"
"6034" "in company with a good fat goose, which is, I have no doubt, roasting"
"6035" "at this moment in front of Peterson’s fire. The facts are these: about"
"6036" "four o’clock on Christmas morning, Peterson, who, as you know, is a"
"6037" "very honest fellow, was returning from some small jollification, and"
"6038" "was making his way homeward down Tottenham Court Road. In front of him"
"6039" "he saw, in the gaslight, a tallish man, walking with a slight stagger,"
"6040" "and carrying a white goose slung over his shoulder. As he reached the"
"6041" "corner of Goodge Street, a row broke out between this stranger and a"
"6042" "little knot of roughs. One of the latter knocked off the man’s hat, on"
"6043" "which he raised his stick to defend himself, and, swinging it over his"
"6044" "head, smashed the shop window behind him. Peterson had rushed forward"
"6045" "to protect the stranger from his assailants; but the man, shocked at"
"6046" "having broken the window, and seeing an official-looking person in"
"6047" "uniform rushing towards him, dropped his goose, took to his heels, and"
"6048" "vanished amid the labyrinth of small streets which lie at the back of"
"6049" "Tottenham Court Road. The roughs had also fled at the appearance of"
"6050" "Peterson, so that he was left in possession of the field of battle, and"
"6051" "also of the spoils of victory in the shape of this battered hat and a"
"6052" "most unimpeachable Christmas goose.”"
"6053" ""
"6054" "“Which surely he restored to their owner?”"
"6055" ""
"6056" "“My dear fellow, there lies the problem. It is true that ‘For Mrs."
"6057" "Henry Baker’ was printed upon a small card which was tied to the bird’s"
"6058" "left leg, and it is also true that the initials ‘H. B.’ are legible"
"6059" "upon the lining of this hat; but as there are some thousands of Bakers,"
"6060" "and some hundreds of Henry Bakers in this city of ours, it is not easy"
"6061" "to restore lost property to any one of them.”"
"6062" ""
"6063" "“What, then, did Peterson do?”"
"6064" ""
"6065" "“He brought round both hat and goose to me on Christmas morning,"
"6066" "knowing that even the smallest problems are of interest to me. The"
"6067" "goose we retained until this morning, when there were signs that, in"
"6068" "spite of the slight frost, it would be well that it should be eaten"
"6069" "without unnecessary delay. Its finder has carried it off, therefore, to"
"6070" "fulfil the ultimate destiny of a goose, while I continue to retain the"
"6071" "hat of the unknown gentleman who lost his Christmas dinner.”"
"6072" ""
"6073" "“Did he not advertise?”"
"6074" ""
"6075" "“No.”"
"6076" ""
"6077" "“Then, what clue could you have as to his identity?”"
"6078" ""
"6079" "“Only as much as we can deduce.”"
"6080" ""
"6081" "“From his hat?”"
"6082" ""
"6083" "“Precisely.”"
"6084" ""
"6085" "“But you are joking. What can you gather from this old battered felt?”"
"6086" ""
"6087" "“Here is my lens. You know my methods. What can you gather yourself as"
"6088" "to the individuality of the man who has worn this article?”"
"6089" ""
"6090" "I took the tattered object in my hands and turned it over rather"
"6091" "ruefully. It was a very ordinary black hat of the usual round shape,"
"6092" "hard, and much the worse for wear. The lining had been of red silk, but"
"6093" "was a good deal discolored. There was no maker’s name; but, as Holmes"
"6094" "had remarked, the initials “H. B.” were scrawled upon one side. It was"
"6095" "pierced in the brim for a hat-securer, but the elastic was missing. For"
"6096" "the rest, it was cracked, exceedingly dusty, and spotted in several"
"6097" "places, although there seemed to have been some attempt to hide the"
"6098" "discolored patches by smearing them with ink."
"6099" ""
"6100" "“I can see nothing,” said I, handing it back to my friend."
"6101" ""

"6904" "Adventure VIII"
"6905" ""
"6906" "THE ADVENTURE OF THE SPECKLED BAND"
"6907" ""
"6908" ""
"6909" "On glancing over my notes of the seventy odd cases in which I have"
"6910" "during the last eight years studied the methods of my friend Sherlock"
"6911" "Holmes, I find many tragic, some comic, a large number merely strange,"
"6912" "but none commonplace; for, working as he did rather for the love of his"
"6913" "art than for the acquirement of wealth, he refused to associate himself"
"6914" "with any investigation which did not tend towards the unusual, and even"
"6915" "the fantastic. Of all these varied cases, however, I cannot recall any"
"6916" "which presented more singular features than that which was associated"
"6917" "with the well-known Surrey family of the Roylotts of Stoke Moran. The"
"6918" "events in question occurred in the early days of my association with"
"6919" "Holmes, when we were sharing rooms as bachelors in Baker Street. It"
"6920" "is possible that I might have placed them upon record before, but a"
"6921" "promise of secrecy was made at the time, from which I have only been"
"6922" "freed during the last month by the untimely death of the lady to whom"
"6923" "the pledge was given. It is perhaps as well that the facts should now"
"6924" "come to light, for I have reasons to know that there are wide-spread"
"6925" "rumors as to the death of Dr. Grimesby Roylott which tend to make the"
"6926" "matter even more terrible than the truth."
"6927" ""
"6928" "It was early in April in the year ’83 that I woke one morning to find"
"6929" "Sherlock Holmes standing, fully dressed, by the side of my bed. He was"
"6930" "a late riser as a rule, and as the clock on the mantel-piece showed"
"6931" "me that it was only a quarter past seven, I blinked up at him in some"
"6932" "surprise, and perhaps just a little resentment, for I was myself"
"6933" "regular in my habits."
"6934" ""
"6935" "“Very sorry to knock you up, Watson,” said he, “but it’s the common lot"
"6936" "this morning. Mrs. Hudson has been knocked up, she retorted upon me,"
"6937" "and I on you.”"
"6938" ""
"6939" "“What is it, then—a fire?”"
"6940" ""
"6941" "“No; a client. It seems that a young lady has arrived in a considerable"
"6942" "state of excitement, who insists upon seeing me. She is waiting now in"
"6943" "the sitting-room. Now, when young ladies wander about the metropolis"
"6944" "at this hour of the morning, and knock sleepy people up out of their"
"6945" "beds, I presume that it is something very pressing which they have to"
"6946" "communicate. Should it prove to be an interesting case, you would, I am"
"6947" "sure, wish to follow it from the outset. I thought, at any rate, that I"
"6948" "should call you and give you the chance.”"
"6949" ""
"6950" "“My dear fellow, I would not miss it for anything.”"
"6951" ""
"6952" "I had no keener pleasure than in following Holmes in his professional"
"6953" "investigations, and in admiring the rapid deductions, as swift as"
"6954" "intuitions, and yet always founded on a logical basis, with which he"
"6955" "unravelled the problems which were submitted to him. I rapidly threw on"
"6956" "my clothes, and was ready in a few minutes to accompany my friend down"
"6957" "to the sitting-room. A lady dressed in black and heavily veiled, who"
"6958" "had been sitting in the window, rose as we entered."
"6959" ""

"7846" ""
"7847" "“That is our signal,” said Holmes, springing to his feet; “it comes"
"7848" "from the middle window.”"
"7849" ""
"7850" "As we passed out he exchanged a few words with the landlord, explaining"

"7856" ""
"7857" "There was little difficulty in entering the grounds, for unrepaired"

"7864" ""

"7870" ""

"7872" ""

"7882" ""
"7883" "“The least sound would be fatal to our plans.”"
"7884" ""
"7885" "I nodded to show that I had heard."
"7886" ""
"7887" "“We must sit without light. He would see it through the ventilator.”"
"7888" ""

"7890" ""

"7894" ""

"7896" ""

"7981" ""
"7982" "       *       *       *       *       *"
"7983" ""
"7984" "Such are the true facts of the death of Dr. Grimesby Roylott, of Stoke"
"7985" "Moran. It is not necessary that I should prolong a narrative which has"
"7986" "already run to too great a length, by telling how we broke the sad news"

"7988" "care of her good aunt at Harrow, of how the slow process of official"
"7989" "inquiry came to the conclusion that the doctor met his fate while"
"7990" "indiscreetly playing with a dangerous pet. The little which I had yet"
"7991" "to learn of the case was told me by Sherlock Holmes as we travelled"
"7992" "back next day."
"7993" ""
"7994" "“I had,” said he, “come to an entirely erroneous conclusion, which"
"7995" "shows, my dear Watson, how dangerous it always is to reason from"
"7996" "insufficient data. The presence of the gypsies, and the use of the"
"7997" "word ‘band,’ which was used by the poor girl, no doubt to explain the"
"7998" "appearance which she had caught a hurried glimpse of by the light of"
"7999" "her match, were sufficient to put me upon an entirely wrong scent. I"
"8000" "can only claim the merit that I instantly reconsidered my position"
"8001" "when, however, it became clear to me that whatever danger threatened"
"8002" "an occupant of the room could not come either from the window or the"
"8003" "door. My attention was speedily drawn, as I have already remarked to"
"8004" "you, to this ventilator, and to the bell-rope which hung down to the"
"8005" "bed. The discovery that this was a dummy, and that the bed was clamped"
"8006" "to the floor, instantly gave rise to the suspicion that the rope was"
"8007" "there as bridge for something passing through the hole, and coming"
"8008" "to the bed. The idea of a snake instantly occurred to me, and when"
"8009" "I coupled it with my knowledge that the doctor was furnished with a"
"8010" "supply of creatures from India, I felt that I was probably on the right"
"8011" "track. The idea of using a form of poison which could not possibly be"
"8012" "discovered by any chemical test was just such a one as would occur to a"
"8013" "clever and ruthless man who had had an Eastern training. The rapidity"
"8014" "with which such a poison would take effect would also, from his point"
"8015" "of view, be an advantage. It would be a sharp-eyed coroner, indeed, who"
"8016" "could distinguish the two little dark punctures which would show where"
"8017" "the poison fangs had done their work. Then I thought of the whistle. Of"
"8018" "course he must recall the snake before the morning light revealed it to"
"8019" "the victim. He had trained it, probably by the use of the milk which"
"8020" "we saw, to return to him when summoned. He would put it through this"
"8021" "ventilator at the hour that he thought best, with the certainty that it"
"8022" "would crawl down the rope and land on the bed. It might or might not"
"8023" "bite the occupant, perhaps she might escape every night for a week, but"
"8024" "sooner or later she must fall a victim."
"8025" ""
"8026" "“I had come to these conclusions before ever I had entered his room."
"8027" "An inspection of his chair showed me that he had been in the habit of"
"8028" "standing on it, which of course would be necessary in order that he"
"8029" "should reach the ventilator. The sight of the safe, the saucer of milk,"
"8030" "and the loop of whip-cord were enough to finally dispel any doubts"
"8031" "which may have remained. The metallic clang heard by Miss Stoner was"
"8032" "obviously caused by her step-father hastily closing the door of his"
"8033" "safe upon its terrible occupant. Having once made up my mind, you know"
"8034" "the steps which I took in order to put the matter to the proof. I"
"8035" "heard the creature hiss, as I have no doubt that you did also, and I"
"8036" "instantly lit the light and attacked it.”"
"8037" ""
"8038" "“With the result of driving it through the ventilator.”"
"8039" ""
"8040" "“And also with the result of causing it to turn upon its master at the"
"8041" "other side. Some of the blows of my cane came home, and roused its"
"8042" "snakish temper, so that it flew upon the first person it saw. In this"

"8044" "death, and I cannot say that it is likely to weigh very heavily upon my"

"8046" ""
"8047" ""
"8048" ""
"8049" ""
"8050" "Adventure IX"
"8051" ""
"8052" "THE ADVENTURE OF THE ENGINEER’S THUMB"
"8053" ""
"8054" ""
"8055" "Of all the problems which have been submitted to my friend Mr. Sherlock"
"8056" "Holmes for solution during the years of our intimacy, there were only"
"8057" "two which I was the means of introducing to his notice—that of Mr."
"8058" "Hatherley’s thumb, and that of Colonel Warburton’s madness. Of these"
"8059" "the latter may have afforded a finer field for an acute and original"
"8060" "observer, but the other was so strange in its inception and so dramatic"
"8061" "in its details, that it may be the more worthy of being placed upon"
"8062" "record, even if it gave my friend fewer openings for those deductive"
"8063" "methods of reasoning by which he achieved such remarkable results. The"
"8064" "story has, I believe, been told more than once in the newspapers, but,"
"8065" "like all such narratives, its effect is much less striking when set"
"8066" "forth _en bloc_ in a single half-column of print than when the facts"
"8067" "slowly evolve before your own eyes, and the mystery clears gradually"
"8068" "away as each new discovery furnishes a step which leads on to the"
"8069" "complete truth. At the time the circumstances made a deep impression"
"8070" "upon me, and the lapse of two years has hardly served to weaken the"
"8071" "effect."
"8072" ""
"8073" "It was in the summer of ’89, not long after my marriage, that the"
"8074" "events occurred which I am now about to summarize. I had returned to"
"8075" "civil practice, and had finally abandoned Holmes in his Baker Street"
"8076" "rooms, although I continually visited him, and occasionally even"
"8077" "persuaded him to forego his Bohemian habits so far as to come and visit"
"8078" "us. My practice had steadily increased, and as I happened to live at"
"8079" "no very great distance from Paddington Station, I got a few patients"
"8080" "from among the officials. One of these, whom I had cured of a painful"
"8081" "and lingering disease, was never weary of advertising my virtues, and"
"8082" "of endeavoring to send me on every sufferer over whom he might have any"
"8083" "influence."
"8084" ""
"8085" "One morning, at a little before seven o’clock, I was awakened by"
"8086" "the maid tapping at the door, to announce that two men had come"
"8087" "from Paddington, and were waiting in the consulting-room. I dressed"
"8088" "hurriedly, for I knew by experience that railway cases were seldom"
"8089" "trivial, and hastened down-stairs. As I descended, my old ally, the"
"8090" "guard, came out of the room and closed the door tightly behind him."
"8091" ""
"8092" "“I’ve got him here,” he whispered, jerking his thumb over his shoulder;"
"8093" "“he’s all right.”"
"8094" ""
"8095" "“What is it, then?” I asked, for his manner suggested that it was some"
"8096" "strange creature which he had caged up in my room."
"8097" ""
"8098" "“It’s a new patient,” he whispered. “I thought I’d bring him round"
"8099" "myself; then he couldn’t slip away. There he is, all safe and sound. I"
"8100" "must go now, doctor; I have my dooties, just the same as you.” And off"
"8101" "he went, this trusty tout, without even giving me time to thank him."
"8102" ""
"8103" "I entered my consulting-room and found a gentleman seated by the"
"8104" "table. He was quietly dressed in a suit of heather tweed, with a soft"
"8105" "cloth cap, which he had laid down upon my books. Round one of his"
"8106" "hands he had a handkerchief wrapped, which was mottled all over with"
"8107" "blood-stains. He was young, not more than five-and-twenty, I should"
"8108" "say, with a strong, masculine face; but he was exceedingly pale, and"
"8109" "gave me the impression of a man who was suffering from some strong"
"8110" "agitation, which it took all his strength of mind to control."
"8111" ""
"8112" "“I am sorry to knock you up so early, doctor,” said he, “but I have"
"8113" "had a very serious accident during the night. I came in by train this"
"8114" "morning, and on inquiring at Paddington as to where I might find a"
"8115" "doctor, a worthy fellow very kindly escorted me here. I gave the maid a"
"8116" "card, but I see that she has left it upon the side-table.”"
"8117" ""
"8118" "I took it up and glanced at it. “Mr. Victor Hatherley, hydraulic"
"8119" "engineer, 16A, Victoria Street (3d floor).” That was the name,"
"8120" "style, and abode of my morning visitor. “I regret that I have kept you"
"8121" "waiting,” said I, sitting down in my library-chair. “You are fresh"
"8122" "from a night journey, I understand, which is in itself a monotonous"
"8123" "occupation.”"
"8124" ""
"8125" "“Oh, my night could not be called monotonous,” said he, and laughed. He"
"8126" "laughed very heartily, with a high, ringing note, leaning back in his"
"8127" "chair and shaking his sides. All my medical instincts rose up against"
"8128" "that laugh."
"8129" ""
"8130" "“Stop it!” I cried; “pull yourself together!” and I poured out some"
"8131" "water from a caraffe."
"8132" ""
"8133" "It was useless, however. He was off in one of those hysterical"
"8134" "outbursts which come upon a strong nature when some great crisis is"
"8135" "over and gone. Presently he came to himself once more, very weary and"
"8136" "blushing hotly."
"8137" ""
"8138" "“I have been making a fool of myself,” he gasped."
"8139" ""
"8140" "“Not at all. Drink this.” I dashed some brandy into the water, and the"
"8141" "color began to come back to his bloodless cheeks."
"8142" ""
"8143" "“That’s better!” said he. “And now, doctor, perhaps you would kindly"
"8144" "attend to my thumb, or rather to the place where my thumb used to be.”"
"8145" ""
"8146" "He unwound the handkerchief and held out his hand. It gave even my"
"8147" "hardened nerves a shudder to look at it. There were four protruding"

"8153" ""

"8158" ""
"8159" "“Excellent! You should have been a surgeon.”"
"8160" ""
"8161" "“It is a question of hydraulics, you see, and came within my own"
"8162" "province.”"
"8163" ""
"8164" "“This has been done,” said I, examining the wound, “by a very heavy and"

"8166" ""
"8167" "“A thing like a cleaver,” said he."
"8168" ""
"8169" "“An accident, I presume?”"
"8170" ""
"8171" "“By no means.”"
"8172" ""
"8173" "“What! a murderous attack?”"
"8174" ""
"8175" "“Very murderous indeed.”"
"8176" ""
"8177" "“You horrify me.”"
"8178" ""
"8179" "I sponged the wound, cleaned it, dressed it, and finally covered it"

"8198" ""
"8199" "“Ha!” cried I, “if it is anything in the nature of a problem which you"

"8202" ""
"8203" "“Oh, I have heard of that fellow,” answered my visitor, “and I should"

"8205" "use the official police as well. Would you give me an introduction to"
"8206" "him?”"
"8207" ""
"8208" "“I’ll do better. I’ll take you round to him myself.”"
"8209" ""
"8210" "“I should be immensely obliged to you.”"
"8211" ""
"8212" "“We’ll call a cab and go together. We shall just be in time to have a"
"8213" "little breakfast with him. Do you feel equal to it?”"
"8214" ""
"8215" "“Yes; I shall not feel easy until I have told my story.”"
"8216" ""
"8217" "“Then my servant will call a cab, and I shall be with you in an"

"8221" ""
"8222" "Sherlock Holmes was, as I expected, lounging about his sitting-room in"

"8224" "his before-breakfast pipe, which was composed of all the plugs and"

"8226" "and collected on the corner of the mantel-piece. He received us in his"

"8229" "upon the sofa, placed a pillow beneath his head, and laid a glass of"

"8231" ""
"8232" "“It is easy to see that your experience has been no common one, Mr."
"8233" "Hatherley,” said he. “Pray, lie down there and make yourself absolutely"
"8234" "at home. Tell us what you can, but stop when you are tired, and keep up"

"8236" ""
"8237" "“Thank you,” said my patient, “but I have felt another man since the"

"8241" ""
"8242" "Holmes sat in his big arm-chair with the weary, heavy-lidded expression"

"8244" "and we listened in silence to the strange story which our visitor"

"8246" ""
"8247" "“You must know,” said he, “that I am an orphan and a bachelor, residing"
"8248" "alone in lodgings in London. By profession I am an hydraulic engineer,"
"8249" "and I have had considerable experience of my work during the seven"
"8250" "years that I was apprenticed to Venner & Matheson, the well-known"
"8251" "firm, of Greenwich. Two years ago, having served my time, and having"
"8252" "also come into a fair sum of money through my poor father’s death,"
"8253" "I determined to start in business for myself, and took professional"
"8254" "chambers in Victoria Street."
"8255" ""
"8256" "“I suppose that every one finds his first independent start in business"
"8257" "a dreary experience. To me it has been exceptionally so. During two"
"8258" "years I have had three consultations and one small job, and that is"

"8260" "amount to £27 10_s._ Every day, from nine in the morning until four in"
"8261" "the afternoon, I waited in my little den, until at last my heart began"
"8262" "to sink, and I came to believe that I should never have any practice at"
"8263" "all."
"8264" ""
"8265" "“Yesterday, however, just as I was thinking of leaving the office,"
"8266" "my clerk entered to say there was a gentleman waiting who wished to"

"8680" "dreadful snap. Easier the other way, perhaps; and yet, had I the nerve"
"8681" "to lie and look up at that deadly black shadow wavering down upon me?"
"8682" "Already I was unable to stand erect, when my eye caught something which"
"8683" "brought a gush of hope back to my heart."
"8684" ""
"8685" "“I have said that though the floor and ceiling were of iron, the walls"
"8686" "were of wood. As I gave a last hurried glance around, I saw a thin"
"8687" "line of yellow light between two of the boards, which broadened and"
"8688" "broadened as a small panel was pushed backward. For an instant I could"
"8689" "hardly believe that here was indeed a door which led away from death."
"8690" "The next instant I threw myself through, and lay half-fainting upon the"
"8691" "other side. The panel had closed again behind me, but the crash of the"
"8692" "lamp, and a few moments afterwards the clang of the two slabs of metal,"
"8693" "told me how narrow had been my escape."
"8694" ""
"8695" "“I was recalled to myself by a frantic plucking at my wrist, and I"
"8696" "found myself lying upon the stone floor of a narrow corridor, while a"
"8697" "woman bent over me and tugged at me with her left hand, while she held"
"8698" "a candle in her right. It was the same good friend whose warning I had"
"8699" "so foolishly rejected."
"8700" ""
"8701" "“‘Come! come!’ she cried, breathlessly. ‘They will be here in a moment."
"8702" "They will see that you are not there. Oh, do not waste the so-precious"
"8703" "time, but come!’"
"8704" ""
"8705" "“This time, at least, I did not scorn her advice. I staggered to my"
"8706" "feet and ran with her along the corridor and down a winding stair. The"
"8707" "latter led to another broad passage, and, just as we reached it, we"
"8708" "heard the sound of running feet and the shouting of two voices, one"
"8709" "answering the other, from the floor on which we were and from the one"
"8710" "beneath. My guide stopped and looked about her like one who is at her"
"8711" "wits’ end. Then she threw open a door which led into a bedroom, through"
"8712" "the window of which the moon was shining brightly."
"8713" ""
"8714" "“‘It is your only chance,’ said she. ‘It is high, but it may be that"
"8715" "you can jump it.’"
"8716" ""
"8717" "“As she spoke a light sprang into view at the further end of the"
"8718" "passage, and I saw the lean figure of Colonel Lysander Stark rushing"
"8719" "forward with a lantern in one hand and a weapon like a butcher’s"
"8720" "cleaver in the other. I rushed across the bedroom, flung open the"
"8721" "window, and looked out. How quiet and sweet and wholesome the garden"
"8722" "looked in the moonlight, and it could not be more than thirty feet"
"8723" "down. I clambered out upon the sill, but I hesitated to jump until I"
"8724" "should have heard what passed between my savior and the ruffian who"
"8725" "pursued me. If she were ill-used, then at any risks I was determined to"
"8726" "go back to her assistance. The thought had hardly flashed through my"
"8727" "mind before he was at the door, pushing his way past her; but she threw"
"8728" "her arms round him and tried to hold him back."
"8729" ""
"8730" "“‘Fritz! Fritz!’ she cried, in English, ‘remember your promise after"
"8731" "the last time. You said it should not be again. He will be silent! Oh,"
"8732" "he will be silent!’"
"8733" ""
"8734" "“‘You are mad, Elise!’ he shouted, struggling to break away from her."
"8735" "‘You will be the ruin of us. He has seen too much. Let me pass, I say!’"
"8736" "He dashed her to one side, and, rushing to the window, cut at me with"
"8737" "his heavy weapon. I had let myself go, and was hanging by the hands to"
"8738" "the sill, when his blow fell. I was conscious of a dull pain, my grip"
"8739" "loosened, and I fell into the garden below."
"8740" ""
"8741" "“I was shaken but not hurt by the fall; so I picked myself up and"
"8742" "rushed off among the bushes as hard as I could run, for I understood"
"8743" "that I was far from being out of danger yet. Suddenly, however, as I"
"8744" "ran, a deadly dizziness and sickness came over me. I glanced down at"
"8745" "my hand, which was throbbing painfully, and then, for the first time,"
"8746" "saw that my thumb had been cut off and that the blood was pouring from"

"8748" "a sudden buzzing in my ears, and next moment I fell in a dead faint"

"8750" ""
"8751" "“How long I remained unconscious I cannot tell. It must have been"
"8752" "a very long time, for the moon had sunk, and a bright morning was"
"8753" "breaking when I came to myself. My clothes were all sodden with dew,"
"8754" "and my coat-sleeve was drenched with blood from my wounded thumb."
"8755" "The smarting of it recalled in an instant all the particulars of my"

"8757" "might hardly yet be safe from my pursuers. But, to my astonishment,"

"8759" "I had been lying in an angle of the hedge close by the high-road, and"
"8760" "just a little lower down was a long building, which proved, upon my"
"8761" "approaching it, to be the very station at which I had arrived upon the"
"8762" "previous night. Were it not for the ugly wound upon my hand, all that"
"8763" "had passed during those dreadful hours might have been an evil dream."
"8764" ""
"8765" "“Half dazed, I went into the station and asked about the morning train."
"8766" "There would be one to Reading in less than an hour. The same porter"
"8767" "was on duty, I found, as had been there when I arrived. I inquired of"
"8768" "him whether he had ever heard of Colonel Lysander Stark. The name was"
"8769" "strange to him. Had he observed a carriage the night before waiting for"
"8770" "me? No, he had not. Was there a police-station anywhere near? There was"
"8771" "one about three miles off."
"8772" ""
"8773" "“It was too far for me to go, weak and ill as I was. I determined to"

"8778" ""

"8783" ""

"8794" ""

"8801" ""
"8802" "Some three hours or so afterwards we were all in the train together,"

"8808" ""

"8812" ""
"8813" "“It was an hour’s good drive.”"
"8814" ""

"8850" "“You are all wrong.”"
"8851" ""

"8858" ""

"8960" ""
"8961" ""
"8962" ""
"8963" ""
"8964" "Adventure X"
"8965" ""
"8966" "THE ADVENTURE OF THE NOBLE BACHELOR"
"8967" ""
"8968" ""
"8969" "The Lord St. Simon marriage, and its curious termination, have long"
"8970" "ceased to be a subject of interest in those exalted circles in which"
"8971" "the unfortunate bridegroom moves. Fresh scandals have eclipsed it,"
"8972" "and their more piquant details have drawn the gossips away from this"
"8973" "four-year-old drama. As I have reason to believe, however, that the"
"8974" "full facts have never been revealed to the general public, and as my"
"8975" "friend Sherlock Holmes had a considerable share in clearing the matter"
"8976" "up, I feel that no memoir of him would be complete without some little"
"8977" "sketch of this remarkable episode."
"8978" ""
"8979" "It was a few weeks before my own marriage, during the days when I was"
"8980" "still sharing rooms with Holmes in Baker Street, that he came home from"
"8981" "an afternoon stroll to find a letter on the table waiting for him."
"8982" "I had remained in-doors all day, for the weather had taken a sudden"
"8983" "turn to rain, with high autumnal winds, and the jezail bullet which I"
"8984" "had brought back in one of my limbs as a relic of my Afghan campaign,"
"8985" "throbbed with dull persistency. With my body in one easy-chair and my"
"8986" "legs upon another, I had surrounded myself with a cloud of newspapers,"
"8987" "until at last, saturated with the news of the day, I tossed them all"
"8988" "aside and lay listless, watching the huge crest and monogram upon the"
"8989" "envelope upon the table, and wondering lazily who my friend’s noble"
"8990" "correspondent could be."
"8991" ""
"8992" "“Here is a very fashionable epistle,” I remarked, as he entered. “Your"
"8993" "morning letters, if I remember right, were from a fish-monger and a"
"8994" "tide-waiter.”"
"8995" ""
"8996" "“Yes, my correspondence has certainly the charm of variety,” he"
"8997" "answered, smiling, “and the humbler are usually the more interesting."
"8998" "This looks like one of those unwelcome social summonses which call upon"
"8999" "a man either to be bored or to lie.”"
"9000" ""
"9001" "He broke the seal and glanced over the contents."
"9002" ""
"9003" "“Oh, come, it may prove to be something of interest after all.”"
"9004" ""
"9005" "“Not social, then?”"
"9006" ""
"9007" "“No, distinctly professional.”"
"9008" ""
"9009" "“And from a noble client?”"
"9010" ""
"9011" "“One of the highest in England.”"
"9012" ""
"9013" "“My dear fellow, I congratulate you.”"
"9014" ""
"9015" "“I assure you, Watson, without affectation, that the status of my"
"9016" "client is a matter of less moment to me than the interest of his case."
"9017" "It is just possible, however, that that also may not be wanting in this"
"9018" "new investigation. You have been reading the papers diligently of late,"
"9019" "have you not?”"
"9020" ""
"9021" "“It looks like it,” said I, ruefully, pointing to a huge bundle in the"
"9022" "corner. “I have had nothing else to do.”"
"9023" ""
"9024" "“It is fortunate, for you will perhaps be able to post me up. I read"
"9025" "nothing except the criminal news and the agony column. The latter is"
"9026" "always instructive. But if you have followed recent events so closely"
"9027" "you must have read about Lord St. Simon and his wedding?”"
"9028" ""
"9029" "“Oh yes, with the deepest interest.”"
"9030" ""
"9031" "“That is well. The letter which I hold in my hand is from Lord St."
"9032" "Simon. I will read it to you, and in return you must turn over these"
"9033" "papers and let me have whatever bears upon the matter. This is what he"
"9034" "says:"
"9035" ""
"9036" "  “‘MY DEAR MR. SHERLOCK HOLMES,—Lord Backwater tells me that I"
"9037" "  may place implicit reliance upon your judgment and discretion."
"9038" "  I have determined, therefore, to call upon you, and to consult"
"9039" "  you in reference to the very painful event which has occurred"
"9040" "  in connection with my wedding. Mr. Lestrade, of Scotland Yard,"
"9041" "  is acting already in the matter, but he assures me that he sees"
"9042" "  no objection to your co-operation, and that he even thinks that"
"9043" "  it might be of some assistance. I will call at four o’clock in"
"9044" "  the afternoon, and, should you have any other engagement at"
"9045" "  that time, I hope that you will postpone it, as this matter is"
"9046" "  of paramount importance.    Yours faithfully,   ST. SIMON.’"
"9047" ""
"9048" "“It is dated from Grosvenor Mansions, written with a quill pen, and the"
"9049" "noble lord has had the misfortune to get a smear of ink upon the outer"
"9050" "side of his right little finger,” remarked Holmes, as he folded up the"
"9051" "epistle."
"9052" ""
"9053" "“He says four o’clock. It is three now. He will be here in an hour.”"
"9054" ""
"9055" "“Then I have just time, with your assistance, to get clear upon the"
"9056" "subject. Turn over those papers, and arrange the extracts in their"
"9057" "order of time, while I take a glance as to who our client is.” He"
"9058" "picked a red-covered volume from a line of books of reference beside"
"9059" "the mantel-piece. “Here he is,” said he, sitting down and flattening it"
"9060" "out upon his knee. “Lord Robert Walsingham de Vere St. Simon, second"
"9061" "son of the Duke of Balmoral—Hum! Arms: Azure, three caltrops in chief"
"9062" "over a fess sable. Born in 1846. He’s forty-one years of age, which"
"9063" "is mature for marriage. Was Undersecretary for the Colonies in a late"
"9064" "Administration. The Duke, his father, was at one time Secretary for"
"9065" "Foreign Affairs. They inherit Plantagenet blood by direct descent, and"
"9066" "Tudor on the distaff side. Ha! Well, there is nothing very instructive"
"9067" "in all this. I think that I must turn to you, Watson, for something"
"9068" "more solid.”"
"9069" ""
"9070" "“I have very little difficulty in finding what I want,” said I, “for"
"9071" "the facts are quite recent, and the matter struck me as remarkable. I"
"9072" "feared to refer them to you, however, as I knew that you had an inquiry"
"9073" "on hand, and that you disliked the intrusion of other matters.”"
"9074" ""
"9075" "“Oh, you mean the little problem of the Grosvenor Square furniture"
"9076" "van. That is quite cleared up now—though, indeed, it was obvious from"
"9077" "the first. Pray give me the results of your newspaper selections.”"
"9078" ""
"9079" "“Here is the first notice which I can find. It is in the personal"
"9080" "column of _The Morning Post_, and dates, as you see, some weeks back."
"9081" "‘A marriage has been arranged,’ it says, ‘and will, if rumor is"
"9082" "correct, very shortly take place, between Lord Robert St. Simon, second"
"9083" "son of the Duke of Balmoral, and Miss Hatty Doran, the only daughter of"
"9084" "Aloysius Doran, Esq., of San Francisco, Cal., U.S.A.’ That is all.”"
"9085" ""
"9086" "“Terse and to the point,” remarked Holmes, stretching his long, thin"
"9087" "legs towards the fire."
"9088" ""
"9089" "“There was a paragraph amplifying this in one of the society papers"
"9090" "of the same week. Ah, here it is. ‘There will soon be a call for"
"9091" "protection in the marriage market, for the present free-trade principle"
"9092" "appears to tell heavily against our home product. One by one the"
"9093" "management of the noble houses of Great Britain is passing into the"
"9094" "hands of our fair cousins from across the Atlantic. An important"
"9095" "addition has been made during the last week to the list of the prizes"
"9096" "which have been borne away by these charming invaders. Lord St. Simon,"
"9097" "who has shown himself for over twenty years proof against the little"
"9098" "god’s arrows, has now definitely announced his approaching marriage"
"9099" "with Miss Hatty Doran, the fascinating daughter of a California"
"9100" "millionaire. Miss Doran, whose graceful figure and striking face"
"9101" "attracted much attention at the Westbury House festivities, is an"
"9102" "only child, and it is currently reported that her dowry will run to"
"9103" "considerably over the six figures, with expectancies for the future."
"9104" "As it is an open secret that the Duke of Balmoral has been compelled"
"9105" "to sell his pictures within the last few years, and as Lord St. Simon"
"9106" "has no property of his own, save the small estate of Birchmoor, it"

"9743" "“Then I’ll tell our story right away,” said the lady. “Frank here and I"
"9744" "met in ’84, in McQuire’s camp, near the Rockies, where pa was working"

"9751" "knowing anything about it. It would only have made him mad to know, so"

"9865" "“The case has been an interesting one,” remarked Holmes, when our"

"9875" "“You were not yourself at fault at all, then?”"
"9876" ""
"9877" "“From the first, two facts were very obvious to me, the one that the"

"9879" "that she had repented of it within a few minutes of returning home."
"9880" "Obviously something had occurred during the morning, then, to cause her"

"9885" "this country that she could hardly have allowed any one to acquire so"

"9891" "Her young womanhood had, I knew, been spent in rough scenes and under"
"9892" "strange conditions. So far I had got before I ever heard Lord St."

"9899" "gone off with a man, and the man was either a lover or was a previous"
"9900" "husband—the chances being in favor of the latter.”"
"9901" ""

"9903" ""

"9941" "Adventure XI"
"9942" ""
"9943" "THE ADVENTURE OF THE BERYL CORONET"
"9944" ""
"9945" ""
"9946" "“Holmes,” said I, as I stood one morning in our bow-window looking down"
"9947" "the street, “here is a madman coming along. It seems rather sad that"
"9948" "his relatives should allow him to come out alone.”"
"9949" ""
"9950" "My friend rose lazily from his arm-chair and stood with his hands in"
"9951" "the pockets of his dressing-gown, looking over my shoulder. It was a"
"9952" "bright, crisp February morning, and the snow of the day before still"
"9953" "lay deep upon the ground, shimmering brightly in the wintry sun. Down"
"9954" "the centre of Baker Street it had been ploughed into a brown crumbly"
"9955" "band by the traffic, but at either side and on the heaped-up edges of"
"9956" "the foot-paths it still lay as white as when it fell. The gray pavement"
"9957" "had been cleaned and scraped, but was still dangerously slippery, so"
"9958" "that there were fewer passengers than usual. Indeed, from the direction"
"9959" "of the Metropolitan Station no one was coming save the single gentleman"
"9960" "whose eccentric conduct had drawn my attention."
"9961" ""
"9962" "He was a man of about fifty, tall, portly, and imposing, with a"
"9963" "massive, strongly marked face and a commanding figure. He was dressed"
"9964" "in a sombre yet rich style, in black frock-coat, shining hat, neat"
"9965" "brown gaiters, and well-cut pearl-gray trousers. Yet his actions were"
"9966" "in absurd contrast to the dignity of his dress and features, for he"
"9967" "was running hard, with occasional little springs, such as a weary man"
"9968" "gives who is little accustomed to set any tax upon his legs. As he ran"
"9969" "he jerked his hands up and down, waggled his head, and writhed his face"
"9970" "into the most extraordinary contortions."
"9971" ""
"9972" "“What on earth can be the matter with him?” I asked. “He is looking up"
"9973" "at the numbers of the houses.”"
"9974" ""
"9975" "“I believe that he is coming here,” said Holmes, rubbing his hands."
"9976" ""
"9977" "“Here?”"
"9978" ""
"9979" "“Yes; I rather think he is coming to consult me professionally. I think"
"9980" "that I recognize the symptoms. Ha! did I not tell you?” As he spoke,"
"9981" "the man, puffing and blowing, rushed at our door and pulled at our bell"
"9982" "until the whole house resounded with the clanging."
"9983" ""
"9984" "A few moments later he was in our room, still puffing, still"
"9985" "gesticulating, but with so fixed a look of grief and despair in his"
"9986" "eyes that our smiles were turned in an instant to horror and pity. For"
"9987" "a while he could not get his words out, but swayed his body and plucked"
"9988" "at his hair like one who has been driven to the extreme limits of his"
"9989" "reason. Then, suddenly springing to his feet, he beat his head against"
"9990" "the wall with such force that we both rushed upon him and tore him away"
