"10861" "gloom, and then closing it once more hurry back to her room, passing"
"10862" "quite close to where he stood hid behind the curtain."
"10863" ""
"10864" "“As long as she was on the scene he could not take any action without"
"10865" "a horrible exposure of the woman whom he loved. But the instant that"
"10866" "she was gone he realized how crushing a misfortune this would be for"
"10867" "you, and how all-important it was to set it right. He rushed down, just"
"10868" "as he was, in his bare feet, opened the window, sprang out into the"
"10869" "snow, and ran down the lane, where he could see a dark figure in the"
"10870" "moonlight. Sir George Burnwell tried to get away, but Arthur caught"
"10871" "him, and there was a struggle between them, your lad tugging at one"
"10872" "side of the coronet, and his opponent at the other. In the scuffle,"
"10873" "your son struck Sir George, and cut him over the eye. Then something"
"10874" "suddenly snapped, and your son, finding that he had the coronet in his"
"10875" "hands, rushed back, closed the window, ascended to your room, and had"
"10876" "just observed that the coronet had been twisted in the struggle, and"
"10877" "was endeavoring to straighten it when you appeared upon the scene.”"
"10878" ""
"10879" "“Is it possible?” gasped the banker."
"10880" ""
"10881" "“You then roused his anger by calling him names at a moment when he"
"10882" "felt that he had deserved your warmest thanks. He could not explain"
"10883" "the true state of affairs without betraying one who certainly deserved"
"10884" "little enough consideration at his hands. He took the more chivalrous"
"10885" "view, however, and preserved her secret.”"
"10886" ""
"10887" "“And that was why she shrieked and fainted when she saw the coronet,”"
"10888" "cried Mr. Holder. “Oh, my God! what a blind fool I have been! And his"
"10889" "asking to be allowed to go out for five minutes! The dear fellow wanted"
"10890" "to see if the missing piece were at the scene of the struggle. How"
"10891" "cruelly I have misjudged him!”"
"10892" ""
"10893" "“When I arrived at the house,” continued Holmes, “I at once went very"
"10894" "carefully round it to observe if there were any traces in the snow"
"10895" "which might help me. I knew that none had fallen since the evening"
"10896" "before, and also that there had been a strong frost to preserve"
"10897" "impressions. I passed along the tradesmen’s path, but found it all"
"10898" "trampled down and indistinguishable. Just beyond it, however, at the"
"10899" "far side of the kitchen door, a woman had stood and talked with a man,"
"10900" "whose round impressions on one side showed that he had a wooden leg."
"10901" "I could even tell that they had been disturbed, for the woman had run"
"10902" "back swiftly to the door, as was shown by the deep toe and light heel"
"10903" "marks, while Wooden-leg had waited a little, and then had gone away."
"10904" "I thought at the time that this might be the maid and her sweetheart,"
"10905" "of whom you had already spoken to me, and inquiry showed it was so."
"10906" "I passed round the garden without seeing anything more than random"
"10907" "tracks, which I took to be the police; but when I got into the stable"
"10908" "lane a very long and complex story was written in the snow in front of"
"10909" "me."
"10910" ""
"10911" "“There was a double line of tracks of a booted man, and a second double"
"10912" "line which I saw with delight belonged to a man with naked feet. I was"
"10913" "at once convinced from what you had told me that the latter was your"
"10914" "son. The first had walked both ways, but the other had run swiftly,"
"10915" "and, as his tread was marked in places over the depression of the boot,"
"10916" "it was obvious that he had passed after the other. I followed them up,"
"10917" "and found that they led to the hall window, where Boots had worn all"
"10918" "the snow away while waiting. Then I walked to the other end, which was"
"10919" "a hundred yards or more down the lane. I saw where Boots had faced"
"10920" "round, where the snow was cut up as though there had been a struggle,"
"10921" "and, finally, where a few drops of blood had fallen, to show me that I"
"10922" "was not mistaken. Boots had then run down the lane, and another little"
"10923" "smudge of blood showed that it was he who had been hurt. When he came"
"10924" "to the high-road at the other end, I found that the pavement had been"
"10925" "cleared, so there was an end to that clew."
"10926" ""
"10927" "“On entering the house, however, I examined, as you remember, the sill"
"10928" "and framework of the hall window with my lens, and I could at once"
"10929" "see that some one had passed out. I could distinguish the outline of"
"10930" "an instep where the wet foot had been placed in coming in. I was then"
"10931" "beginning to be able to form an opinion as to what had occurred. A man"
"10932" "had waited outside the window, some one had brought the gems; the deed"
"10933" "had been overseen by your son, he had pursued the thief, had struggled"
"10934" "with him, they had each tugged at the coronet, their united strength"
"10935" "causing injuries which neither alone could have effected. He had"
"10936" "returned with the prize, but had left a fragment in the grasp of his"
"10937" "opponent. So far I was clear. The question now was, who was the man,"
"10938" "and who was it brought him the coronet?"
"10939" ""
"10940" "“It is an old maxim of mine that when you have excluded the impossible,"
"10941" "whatever remains, however improbable, must be the truth. Now, I knew"
"10942" "that it was not you who had brought it down, so there only remained"
"10943" "your niece and the maids. But if it were the maids, why should your son"
"10944" "allow himself to be accused in their place? There could be no possible"
"10945" "reason. As he loved his cousin, however, there was an excellent"
"10946" "explanation why he should retain her secret—the more so as the secret"
"10947" "was a disgraceful one. When I remembered that you had seen her at"
"10948" "that window, and how she had fainted on seeing the coronet again, my"
"10949" "conjecture became a certainty."
"10950" ""
"10951" "“And who could it be who was her confederate? A lover evidently, for"
"10952" "who else could outweigh the love and gratitude which she must feel to"
"10953" "you? I knew that you went out little, and that your circle of friends"
"10954" "was a very limited one. But among them was Sir George Burnwell. I had"
"10955" "heard of him before as being a man of evil reputation among women. It"
"10956" "must have been he who wore those boots and retained the missing gems."
"10957" "Even though he knew that Arthur had discovered him, he might still"
"10958" "flatter himself that he was safe, for the lad could not say a word"
"10959" "without compromising his own family."
"10960" ""
"10961" "“Well, your own good sense will suggest what measures I took next. I"
"10962" "went in the shape of a loafer to Sir George’s house, managed to pick"
"10963" "up an acquaintance with his valet, learned that his master had cut his"
"10964" "head the night before, and, finally, at the expense of six shillings,"
"10965" "made all sure by buying a pair of his cast-off shoes. With these I"
"10966" "journeyed down to Streatham, and saw that they exactly fitted the"
"10967" "tracks.”"
"10968" ""
"10969" "[Illustration: “I CLAPPED A PISTOL TO HIS HEAD”]"
"10970" ""
"10971" "“I saw an ill-dressed vagabond in the lane yesterday evening,” said Mr."
"10972" "Holder."
"10973" ""
"10974" "“Precisely. It was I. I found that I had my man, so I came home and"
"10975" "changed my clothes. It was a delicate part which I had to play then,"
"10976" "for I saw that a prosecution must be avoided to avert scandal, and I"
"10977" "knew that so astute a villain would see that our hands were tied in the"
"10978" "matter. I went and saw him. At first, of course, he denied everything."
"10979" "But when I gave him every particular that had occurred, he tried to"
"10980" "bluster, and took down a life-preserver from the wall. I knew my man,"
"10981" "however, and I clapped a pistol to his head before he could strike."
"10982" "Then he became a little more reasonable. I told him that we would give"
"10983" "him a price for the stones he held—£1000 apiece. That brought out the"
"10984" "first signs of grief that he had shown. ‘Why, dash it all!’ said he,"
"10985" "‘I’ve let them go at six hundred for the three!’ I soon managed to get"
"10986" "the address of the receiver who had them, on promising him that there"
"10987" "would be no prosecution. Off I set to him, and after much chaffering I"
"10988" "got our stones at £1000 apiece. Then I looked in upon your son, told"
"10989" "him that all was right, and eventually got to my bed about two o’clock,"
"10990" "after what I may call a really hard day’s work.”"
"10991" ""
"10992" "“A day which has saved England from a great public scandal,” said the"
"10993" "banker, rising. “Sir, I cannot find words to thank you, but you shall"
"10994" "not find me ungrateful for what you have done. Your skill has indeed"
"10995" "exceeded all that I have heard of it. And now I must fly to my dear boy"
"10996" "to apologize to him for the wrong which I have done him. As to what you"
"10997" "tell me of poor Mary, it goes to my very heart. Not even your skill can"
"10998" "inform me where she is now.”"
"10999" ""
"11000" "“I think that we may safely say,” returned Holmes, “that she is"
"11001" "wherever Sir George Burnwell is. It is equally certain, too, that"
"11002" "whatever her sins are, they will soon receive a more than sufficient"
"11003" "punishment.”"

"11008" "Adventure XII"
"11009" ""
"11010" "THE ADVENTURE OF THE COPPER BEECHES"
"11011" ""
"11012" ""
"11013" "“To the man who loves art for its own sake,” remarked Sherlock Holmes,"
"11014" "tossing aside the advertisement sheet of _The Daily Telegraph_, “it is"
"11015" "frequently in its least important and lowliest manifestations that the"
"11016" "keenest pleasure is to be derived. It is pleasant to me to observe,"
"11017" "Watson, that you have so far grasped this truth that in these little"
"11018" "records of our cases which you have been good enough to draw up, and, I"
"11019" "am bound to say, occasionally to embellish, you have given prominence"
"11020" "not so much to the many _causes célèbres_ and sensational trials in"
"11021" "which I have figured, but rather to those incidents which may have been"
"11022" "trivial in themselves, but which have given room for those faculties"
"11023" "of deduction and of logical synthesis which I have made my special"
"11024" "province.”"
"11025" ""
"11026" "“And yet,” said I, smiling, “I cannot quite hold myself absolved from"
"11027" "the charge of sensationalism which has been urged against my records.”"
"11028" ""
"11029" "“You have erred, perhaps,” he observed, taking up a glowing cinder with"
"11030" "the tongs, and lighting with it the long cherry-wood pipe which was"
"11031" "wont to replace his clay when he was in a disputatious, rather than a"
"11032" "meditative mood—“you have erred perhaps in attempting to put color and"
"11033" "life into each of your statements, instead of confining yourself to the"
"11034" "task of placing upon record that severe reasoning from cause to effect"
"11035" "which is really the only notable feature about the thing.”"
"11036" ""
"11037" "“It seems to me that I have done you full justice in the matter,” I"
"11038" "remarked, with some coldness, for I was repelled by the egotism which"
"11039" "I had more than once observed to be a strong factor in my friend’s"
"11040" "singular character."
"11041" ""
"11042" "“No, it is not selfishness or conceit,” said he, answering, as was his"
"11043" "wont, my thoughts rather than my words. “If I claim full justice for my"
"11044" "art, it is because it is an impersonal thing—a thing beyond myself."
"11045" "Crime is common. Logic is rare. Therefore it is upon the logic rather"
"11046" "than upon the crime that you should dwell. You have degraded what"
"11047" "should have been a course of lectures into a series of tales.”"
"11048" ""
"11049" "It was a cold morning of the early spring, and we sat after breakfast"
"11050" "on either side of a cheery fire in the old room at Baker Street. A"
"11051" "thick fog rolled down between the lines of dun-colored houses, and the"
"11052" "opposing windows loomed like dark, shapeless blurs through the heavy"
"11053" "yellow wreaths. Our gas was lit, and shone on the white cloth and"
"11054" "glimmer of china and metal, for the table had not been cleared yet."
"11055" "Sherlock Holmes had been silent all the morning, dipping continuously"
"11056" "into the advertisement columns of a succession of papers, until at"
"11057" "last, having apparently given up his search, he had emerged in no very"
"11058" "sweet temper to lecture me upon my literary shortcomings."
"11059" ""
"11060" "“At the same time,” he remarked, after a pause, during which he had sat"
"11061" "puffing at his long pipe and gazing down into the fire, “you can hardly"
"11062" "be open to a charge of sensationalism, for out of these cases which you"
"11063" "have been so kind as to interest yourself in, a fair proportion do not"
"11064" "treat of crime, in its legal sense, at all. The small matter in which I"
"11065" "endeavored to help the King of Bohemia, the singular experience of Miss"
"11066" "Mary Sutherland, the problem connected with the man with the twisted"
"11067" "lip, and the incident of the noble bachelor, were all matters which are"
"11068" "outside the pale of the law. But in avoiding the sensational, I fear"
"11069" "that you may have bordered on the trivial.”"
"11070" ""
"11071" "“The end may have been so,” I answered, “but the methods I hold to have"
"11072" "been novel and of interest.”"
"11073" ""
"11074" "“Pshaw, my dear fellow, what do the public, the great unobservant"
"11075" "public, who could hardly tell a weaver by his tooth or a compositor by"
"11076" "his left thumb, care about the finer shades of analysis and deduction!"
"11077" "But, indeed, if you are trivial, I cannot blame you, for the days of"
"11078" "the great cases are past. Man, or at least criminal man, has lost all"
"11079" "enterprise and originality. As to my own little practice, it seems to"
"11080" "be degenerating into an agency for recovering lost lead pencils and"
"11081" "giving advice to young ladies from boarding-schools. I think that I"
"11082" "have touched bottom at last, however. This note I had this morning"
"11083" "marks my zero-point, I fancy. Read it!” He tossed a crumpled letter"
"11084" "across to me."
"11085" ""
"11086" "It was dated from Montague Place upon the preceding evening, and ran"

"11088" ""

"11689" "upon the other side. That dreadful silent sentinel sent a chill to my"
"11690" "heart which I do not think that any burglar could have done."
"11691" ""
"11692" "“And now I have a very strange experience to tell you. I had, as you"
"11693" "know, cut off my hair in London, and I had placed it in a great coil"
"11694" "at the bottom of my trunk. One evening, after the child was in bed,"
"11695" "I began to amuse myself by examining the furniture of my room and by"
"11696" "rearranging my own little things. There was an old chest of drawers"
"11697" "in the room, the two upper ones empty and open, the lower one locked."
"11698" "I had filled the first two with my linen, and, as I had still much"
"11699" "to pack away, I was naturally annoyed at not having the use of the"
"11700" "third drawer. It struck me that it might have been fastened by a mere"
"11701" "oversight, so I took out my bunch of keys and tried to open it. The"
"11702" "very first key fitted to perfection, and I drew the drawer open. There"
"11703" "was only one thing in it, but I am sure that you would never guess what"
"11704" "it was. It was my coil of hair."
"11705" ""
"11706" "“I took it up and examined it. It was of the same peculiar tint, and"
"11707" "the same thickness. But then the impossibility of the thing obtruded"
"11708" "itself upon me. How _could_ my hair have been locked in the drawer?"
"11709" "With trembling hands I undid my trunk, turned out the contents, and"
"11710" "drew from the bottom my own hair. I laid the two tresses together, and"
"11711" "I assure you that they were identical. Was it not extraordinary? Puzzle"
"11712" "as I would, I could make nothing at all of what it meant. I returned"
"11713" "the strange hair to the drawer, and I said nothing of the matter to the"
"11714" "Rucastles, as I felt that I had put myself in the wrong by opening a"
"11715" "drawer which they had locked."
"11716" ""
"11717" "“I am naturally observant, as you may have remarked, Mr. Holmes, and I"
"11718" "soon had a pretty good plan of the whole house in my head. There was"
"11719" "one wing, however, which appeared not to be inhabited at all. A door"
"11720" "which faced that which led into the quarters of the Tollers opened"
"11721" "into this suite, but it was invariably locked. One day, however, as I"
"11722" "ascended the stair, I met Mr. Rucastle coming out through this door,"
"11723" "his keys in his hand, and a look on his face which made him a very"
"11724" "different person to the round, jovial man to whom I was accustomed. His"
"11725" "cheeks were red, his brow was all crinkled with anger, and the veins"
"11726" "stood out at his temples with passion. He locked the door and hurried"
"11727" "past me without a word or a look."
"11728" ""
"11729" "“This aroused my curiosity; so when I went out for a walk in the"
"11730" "grounds with my charge, I strolled round to the side from which I could"
"11731" "see the windows of this part of the house. There were four of them in a"
"11732" "row, three of which were simply dirty, while the fourth was shuttered"
"11733" "up. They were evidently all deserted. As I strolled up and down,"
"11734" "glancing at them occasionally, Mr. Rucastle came out to me, looking as"
"11735" "merry and jovial as ever."
"11736" ""
"11737" "“‘Ah!’ said he, ‘you must not think me rude if I passed you without a"
"11738" "word, my dear young lady. I was preoccupied with business matters.’"
"11739" ""
"11740" "“I assured him that I was not offended. ‘By-the-way,’ said I, ‘you"
"11741" "seem to have quite a suite of spare rooms up there, and one of them has"
"11742" "the shutters up.’"
"11743" ""
"11744" "“He looked surprised, and, as it seemed to me, a little startled at my"
"11745" "remark."
"11746" ""
"11747" "“‘Photography is one of my hobbies,’ said he. ‘I have made my dark room"
"11748" "up there. But, dear me! what an observant young lady we have come upon."
"11749" "Who would have believed it? Who would have ever believed it?’ He spoke"
"11750" "in a jesting tone, but there was no jest in his eyes as he looked at"
"11751" "me. I read suspicion there and annoyance, but no jest."
"11752" ""
"11753" "“Well, Mr. Holmes, from the moment that I understood that there was"
"11754" "something about that suite of rooms which I was not to know, I was all"
"11755" "on fire to go over them. It was not mere curiosity, though I have my"
"11756" "share of that. It was more a feeling of duty—a feeling that some good"
"11757" "might come from my penetrating to this place. They talk of woman’s"
"11758" "instinct; perhaps it was woman’s instinct which gave me that feeling."
"11759" "At any rate, it was there, and I was keenly on the lookout for any"
"11760" "chance to pass the forbidden door."
"11761" ""
"11762" "“It was only yesterday that the chance came. I may tell you that,"
"11763" "besides Mr. Rucastle, both Toller and his wife find something to do in"
"11764" "these deserted rooms, and I once saw him carrying a large black linen"
"11765" "bag with him through the door. Recently he has been drinking hard, and"
"11766" "yesterday evening he was very drunk; and, when I came up-stairs, there"
"11767" "was the key in the door. I have no doubt at all that he had left it"
"11768" "there. Mr. and Mrs. Rucastle were both down-stairs, and the child was"
"11769" "with them, so that I had an admirable opportunity. I turned the key"
"11770" "gently in the lock, opened the door, and slipped through."
"11771" ""
"11772" "“There was a little passage in front of me, unpapered and uncarpeted,"
"11773" "which turned at a right angle at the farther end. Round this corner"
"11774" "were three doors in a line, the first and third of which were open."
"11775" "They each led into an empty room, dusty and cheerless, with two windows"
"11776" "in the one and one in the other, so thick with dirt that the evening"
"11777" "light glimmered dimly through them. The centre door was closed, and"
"11778" "across the outside of it had been fastened one of the broad bars of"
"11779" "an iron bed, padlocked at one end to a ring in the wall, and fastened"
"11780" "at the other with stout cord. The door itself was locked as well, and"
"11781" "the key was not there. This barricaded door corresponded clearly with"
"11782" "the shuttered window outside, and yet I could see by the glimmer from"
"11783" "beneath it that the room was not in darkness. Evidently there was a"
"11784" "skylight which let in light from above. As I stood in the passage"
"11785" "gazing at the sinister door, and wondering what secret it might veil,"
"11786" "I suddenly heard the sound of steps within the room, and saw a shadow"
"11787" "pass backward and forward against the little slit of dim light which"
"11788" "shone out from under the door. A mad, unreasoning terror rose up in"
"11789" "me at the sight, Mr. Holmes. My overstrung nerves failed me suddenly,"
"11790" "and I turned and ran—ran as though some dreadful hand were behind me"
"11791" "clutching at the skirt of my dress. I rushed down the passage, through"
"11792" "the door, and straight into the arms of Mr. Rucastle, who was waiting"
"11793" "outside."
"11794" ""
"11795" "“‘So,’ said he, smiling, ‘it was you, then. I thought that it must be"
"11796" "when I saw the door open.’"
"11797" ""
"11798" "“‘Oh, I am so frightened!’ I panted."
"11799" ""
"11800" "“‘My dear young lady! my dear young lady!’—you cannot think how"
"11801" "caressing and soothing his manner was—‘and what has frightened you, my"
"11802" "dear young lady?’"
"11803" ""
"11804" "“But his voice was just a little too coaxing. He overdid it. I was"
"11805" "keenly on my guard against him."
"11806" ""
"11807" "“‘I was foolish enough to go into the empty wing,’ I answered. ‘But it"
"11808" "is so lonely and eerie in this dim light that I was frightened and ran"
"11809" "out again. Oh, it is so dreadfully still in there!’"
"11810" ""
"11811" "“‘Only that?’ said he, looking at me keenly."
"11812" ""
"11813" "“‘Why, what did you think?’ I asked."
"11814" ""
"11815" "“‘Why do you think that I lock this door?’"
"11816" ""
"11817" "“‘I am sure that I do not know.’"
"11818" ""
"11819" "“‘It is to keep people out who have no business there. Do you see?’ He"
"11820" "was still smiling in the most amiable manner."
"11821" ""
"11822" "“‘I am sure if I had known—’"
"11823" ""
"11824" "“‘Well, then, you know now. And if you ever put your foot over that"

"11826" "rage, and he glared down at me with the face of a demon—‘I’ll throw"
"11827" "you to the mastiff.’"
"11828" ""
"11829" "“I was so terrified that I do not know what I did. I suppose that I"
"11830" "must have rushed past him into my room. I remember nothing until I"
"11831" "found myself lying on my bed trembling all over. Then I thought of you,"
"11832" "Mr. Holmes. I could not live there longer without some advice. I was"
"11833" "frightened of the house, of the man, of the woman, of the servants,"
"11834" "even of the child. They were all horrible to me. If I could only bring"
"11835" "you down all would be well. Of course I might have fled from the house,"
"11836" "but my curiosity was almost as strong as my fears. My mind was soon"
"11837" "made up. I would send you a wire. I put on my hat and cloak, went down"
"11838" "to the office, which is about half a mile from the house, and then"
"11839" "returned, feeling very much easier. A horrible doubt came into my mind"
"11840" "as I approached the door lest the dog might be loose, but I remembered"
"11841" "that Toller had drunk himself into a state of insensibility that"
"11842" "evening, and I knew that he was the only one in the household who had"
"11843" "any influence with the savage creature, or who would venture to set him"
"11844" "free. I slipped in in safety, and lay awake half the night in my joy at"
"11845" "the thought of seeing you. I had no difficulty in getting leave to come"
"11846" "into Winchester this morning, but I must be back before three o’clock,"
"11847" "for Mr. and Mrs. Rucastle are going on a visit, and will be away all"
"11848" "the evening, so that I must look after the child. Now I have told you"
"11849" "all my adventures, Mr. Holmes, and I should be very glad if you could"
"11850" "tell me what it all means, and, above all, what I should do.”"
"11851" ""
"11852" "Holmes and I had listened spellbound to this extraordinary story. My"
"11853" "friend rose now and paced up and down the room, his hands in his"
"11854" "pockets, and an expression of the most profound gravity upon his face."
"11855" ""
"11856" "“Is Toller still drunk?” he asked."
"11857" ""
"11858" "“Yes. I heard his wife tell Mrs. Rucastle that she could do nothing"
"11859" "with him.”"
"11860" ""
"11861" "“That is well. And the Rucastles go out to-night?”"
"11862" ""
"11863" "“Yes.”"
"11864" ""
"11865" "“Is there a cellar with a good strong lock?”"
"11866" ""
"11867" "“Yes, the wine-cellar.”"
"11868" ""
"11869" "“You seem to me to have acted all through this matter like a very brave"
"11870" "and sensible girl, Miss Hunter. Do you think that you could perform one"
"11871" "more feat? I should not ask it of you if I did not think you a quite"
"11872" "exceptional woman.”"
"11873" ""
"11874" "“I will try. What is it?”"
"11875" ""
"11876" "“We shall be at the Copper Beeches by seven o’clock, my friend and I."
"11877" "The Rucastles will be gone by that time, and Toller will, we hope, be"
"11878" "incapable. There only remains Mrs. Toller, who might give the alarm. If"
"11879" "you could send her into the cellar on some errand, and then turn the"
"11880" "key upon her, you would facilitate matters immensely.”"
"11881" ""
"11882" "“I will do it.”"
"11883" ""
"11884" "“Excellent! We shall then look thoroughly into the affair. Of course"
"11885" "there is only one feasible explanation. You have been brought there to"
"11886" "personate some one, and the real person is imprisoned in this chamber."
"11887" "That is obvious. As to who this prisoner is, I have no doubt that it is"
"11888" "the daughter, Miss Alice Rucastle, if I remember right, who was said"
"11889" "to have gone to America. You were chosen, doubtless, as resembling her"
"11890" "in height, figure, and the color of your hair. Hers had been cut off,"
"11891" "very possibly in some illness through which she has passed, and so, of"
"11892" "course, yours had to be sacrificed also. By a curious chance you came"
"11893" "upon her tresses. The man in the road was, undoubtedly, some friend of"
"11894" "hers—possibly her _fiancé_—and no doubt, as you wore the girl’s dress"
"11895" "and were so like her, he was convinced from your laughter, whenever"
"11896" "he saw you, and afterwards from your gesture, that Miss Rucastle was"
"11897" "perfectly happy, and that she no longer desired his attentions. The dog"
"11898" "is let loose at night to prevent him from endeavoring to communicate"
"11899" "with her. So much is fairly clear. The most serious point in the case"
"11900" "is the disposition of the child.”"
"11901" ""
"11902" "“What on earth has that to do with it?” I ejaculated."
"11903" ""
"11904" "“My dear Watson, you as a medical man are continually gaining light as"
"11905" "to the tendencies of a child by the study of the parents. Don’t you see"
"11906" "that the converse is equally valid. I have frequently gained my first"
"11907" "real insight into the character of parents by studying their children."
"11908" "This child’s disposition is abnormally cruel, merely for cruelty’s"
"11909" "sake, and whether he derives this from his smiling father, as I should"
"11910" "suspect, or from his mother, it bodes evil for the poor girl who is in"

"11912" ""
"11913" "“I am sure that you are right, Mr. Holmes,” cried our client. “A"
"11914" "thousand things come back to me which make me certain that you have"
"11915" "hit it. Oh, let us lose not an instant in bringing help to this poor"

"11917" ""
"11918" "“We must be circumspect, for we are dealing with a very cunning man. We"

"11921" ""
"11922" "We were as good as our word, for it was just seven when we reached the"

"11927" ""
"11928" "“Have you managed it?” asked Holmes."
"11929" ""
"11930" "A loud thudding noise came from somewhere down-stairs. “That is"

"11932" "the kitchen rug. Here are his keys, which are the duplicates of Mr."

"11934" ""

"11957" ""
"11958" "“Through the skylight. We shall soon see how he managed it.” He swung"

"11961" ""
"11962" "“But it is impossible,” said Miss Hunter; “the ladder was not there"

"11964" ""

"11969" ""

"11974" ""

"12041" ""

"12046" ""
"12047" "“Yes, sir.”"
"12048" ""

"12051" ""
"12052" "“That was it, sir.”"
"12053" ""
"12054" "“But Mr. Fowler being a persevering man, as a good seaman should"
"12055" "be, blockaded the house, and, having met you, succeeded by certain"

"12058" ""
"12059" "“Mr. Fowler was a very kind-spoken, free-handed gentleman,” said Mrs."
"12060" "Toller, serenely."
"12061" ""
"12062" "“And in this way he managed that your good man should have no want of"

"12065" ""

"12067" ""
"12068" "“I am sure we owe you an apology, Mrs. Toller,” said Holmes, “for you"

"12070" "the country surgeon and Mrs. Rucastle, so I think, Watson, that we had"
"12071" "best escort Miss Hunter back to Winchester, as it seems to me that our"
"12072" "_locus standi_ now is rather a questionable one.”"
"12073" ""
"12074" "And thus was solved the mystery of the sinister house with the copper"
"12075" "beeches in front of the door. Mr. Rucastle survived, but was always a"
"12076" "broken man, kept alive solely through the care of his devoted wife."
"12077" "They still live with their old servants, who probably know so much of"
"12078" "Rucastle’s past life that he finds it difficult to part from them."
"12079" "Mr. Fowler and Miss Rucastle were married, by special license, in"
"12080" "Southampton the day after their flight, and he is now the holder of a"
"12081" "Government appointment in the Island of Mauritius. As to Miss Violet"
"12082" "Hunter, my friend Holmes, rather to my disappointment, manifested no"
"12083" "further interest in her when once she had ceased to be the centre of"
"12084" "one of his problems, and she is now the head of a private school at"
"12085" "Walsall, where I believe that she has met with considerable success."

"12155" "their profusion of picturesque description, and their quiet and"

"12157" "atmosphere which diffuses a cheery feeling of healthful and robust"

"12257" "    Two Volumes. Twenty Full-page Photogravures. Over 1000"

"12262" ""
"12263" "Anything so startling, new, and distinctive as the leading feature of"
"12264" "this romance does not often appear in works of fiction.... Some of Mr."
"12265" "Wallace’s writing is remarkable for its pathetic eloquence. The scenes"
"12266" "described in the New Testament are rewritten with the power and skill"
"12267" "of an accomplished master of style.—_N. Y. Times._"
"12268" ""
"12269" "Its real basis is a description of the life of the Jews and Romans"
"12270" "at the beginning of the Christian era, and this is both forcible and"
"12271" "brilliant.... We are carried through a surprising variety of scenes;"
"12272" "we witness a sea-fight, a chariot-race, the internal economy of a"
"12273" "Roman galley, domestic interiors at Antioch, at Jerusalem, and among"
"12274" "the tribes of the desert; palaces, prisons, the haunts of dissipated"
"12275" "Roman youth, the houses of pious families of Israel. There is plenty of"
"12276" "exciting incident; everything is animated, vivid and glowing.—_N. Y."
"12277" "Tribune._"
"12278" ""
"12279" "From the opening of the volume to the very close the reader’s interest"
"12280" "will be kept at the highest pitch, and the novel will be pronounced by"
"12281" "all one of the greatest novels of the day.—_Boston Post._"
"12282" ""
"12283" "“Ben Hur” is interesting, and its characterization is fine and strong."
"12284" "Meanwhile it evinces careful study of the period in which the scene"
"12285" "is laid, and will help those who read it with reasonable attention to"
"12286" "realize the nature and conditions of Hebrew life in Jerusalem and Roman"
"12287" "life at Antioch at the time of our Saviour’s advent.—_Examiner_, N. Y."
"12288" ""
"12289" "The book is one of unquestionable power, and will be read with unwonted"
"12290" "interest by many readers who are weary of the conventional novel and"
"12291" "romance.—_Boston Journal._"
"12292" ""
"12293" "One of the most remarkable and delightful books. It is as real and"
"12294" "warm as life itself, and as attractive as the grandest and most heroic"
"12295" "chapters of history.—_Indianapolis Journal._"
